⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب القسمة
مسائل القسمة
ويقسم العروض من جنس واحد ولا يقسم الجنسان والجواهر والرقيق والحمام جبرا والبئر والرحى إلا برضائهم . دُور مشتركة أو دار وضيعة أو دار وحانوت قسم كل بين اثنين أو أكثر
ويقسم العروض إلخ : أي يقسم العروض إذا كانت من جنس واحد جبرا؛ لأن اعتبار المبادلة في المنفعة المالية ممكن عند اتحاد الجنس؛ لاتحاد المقصود فيه، فيقع تمييزا، فيملك القاضي الإجبار عليها تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٩٨/٨] ولا يقسم إلخ: أي لا يقسم الجنسان والجواهر وما عطف عليهما من الرقيق والحمام والبئر والرحى إلا برضاء الشركاء، فقوله: "إلا "برضائهم" متعلق بالجميع يعني لا يملك القاضي الإجبار على قسمة الجنسين بأن يقسم الأجناس المختلفة قسمة بأن يجمع نصيب أحدهم في الإبل والآخر في البقر ؛ لما في ذلك من تفويت جنس المنفعة على الآبي؛ لأن قبل القسمة كان له المنفعة في الجنسين جميعا، وبعد القسمة فات منفعة أحدهما، فلم تقع القسمة تمييزا بل معاوضة، وهي لا تجوز إلا بالتراضي.
جمع
عدم
فإن قيل: شرط صحة القسمة أن ينتفع بالمقسوم كما كان قبل القسمة؟ قلت: ذاك شرط الجبر عليها لا شرط القسمة بالتراضي، وكذا لا يقسم الجواهر جبرا؛ لفحش التفاوت، ولأن جهالة الجواهر أفحش من جهالة الرقيق، ولهذا لو تزوج على لؤلؤة أو ياقوتة، أو خالع عليها لا تصح التسمية، ولو تزوج أو خالع على عبد يصح، فأولى أن لا يجبر على القسمة، وقيل: لا يقسم الكبار منها؛ لفحش التفاوت ويقسم الصغار؛ لقلة التفاوت، وقيل: إن اختلف جنسهما لا يقسم، وإن اتحد يقسم كسائر الأجناس. (فتح، تكملة بتوضيح واختصار) والرقيق: أي لا يقسم الرقيق أيضا من غير تراض عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يجوز؛ لاتحاد الجنس، فصار كالإبل والخيل والغنم، وبه قالت الثلاثة، وله: أن قسمة الرقيق متعذر لمعانيها الباطنة ولا وقوف عليها، ولا يمكن التعديل، فلا يقسم إلا بتراض، وهذا الخلاف فيما إذا كان الرقيق وحدهم وليس معهم شيء آخر من العروض، وهم ذكور فقط، أو إناث فقط، وأما إذا كانوا مختلطين بين الذكور والإناث لا يقسم بالإجماع، وإن كان مع الرقيق شيء آخر مما يقسم، جازت القسمة في الرقيق تبعا لغيرهم بالإجماع. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٤٩/٢] والحمام إلخ أي لا تقسم هذه الثلاثة إلا برضائهم لما ذكر من إلحاق الضرر بالكل، ولو اقتسما الحمام أو البئر بأنفسهم جاز، ولكل واحد نوع منفعة بأن يتخذ نصيبه من الحمام بيتا وإن طلبا جميعا القسمة من القاضي هل يقسم؟ فيه روايتان في رواية لا يقسم؛ لأنها تضمنت تفويت منفعة، وليس للقاضي ذلك؛ لأنه يكون سفها يمكنه، وفي رواية: يقسم؛ لأنهم رضوا بذلك، وإليه أشار في الكتاب؛ لأنه فيه نوع منفعة كذا في "المحيط". تكملة البحر الرائق: ۲۹۹/۸] إلا برضائهم : متعلق بالمسائل الست المذكورة من قوله: "ولا يقسم". دور مشتركة إلخ : أي إذا كانت دور مشتركة بين اثنين أو أكثر، أو دار وضيعة أو دار وحانوت مشتركة، قسم كل واحد من الدور أو من الدار والضيعة أو من الدار والحانوت على حدة، ولا تقسم قسمة واحدة، أما الدور المشتركة: فالمذكور قول أبي حنيفة، فإنه إذا كان لرجلين دور أو داران في مصر واحد، ولو كانت متلازقة - قال: أي يسويه على سهام القسمة لأن المالية تعرف بالتقويم على حدة، ويصور القاسم ما يقسمه ويعدّله ويذرعه ويقوم البناء، ويفرز كل ولا تقسم قسمة واحدة نصيب بطريقه وشربه ويلقب الأنصباء بالأول والثاني والثالث، ويكتب أساميهم = جمع نصيب والرابع وهلم جرا أسامي الشركاء أو متباينة في محلة أو محلتين وطلبا من القاضي قسمتهما، فإنه يقسم كل دار على حدة، ولا يقسمها قسمة واحدة إلا بتراضيهما. وقالا: إن رأى القسمة أصلح يقسم بعضها في بعض؛ لأنها من جنس واحد، فصار كبيتين في دار واحدة، وله: أنها تتفاوت بالمكان والجيران تفاوتا فاحشا ومبناها على التساوي، وعلى هذا الخلاف الأراضي المشتركة والدور في مصرين لا تقسم بالإجماع فيما رواه هلال وعن محمد أنها تقسم، وأما الدار والضيعة أو الدار والحانوت، فلاختلاف الجنس فيتوهم فيه الربا رمز الحقائق: ٣٤٩/٢]
ويصور القاسم: أي يكتب على قرطاس؛ ليمكنه حفظه، قال في "العناية": يكتب أن نصيب فلان كذا، وفلان كذا إن أرادوا رفع تلك الكاغذة إلى القاضي؛ ليتولى الإقراع بينهم بنفسه. [ تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٠٠/٨] ويذرعه: لأن قدر الساحة يعرف بالذرع، والمالية بالتقويم، ولابد من معرفتها؛ ليمكنه التسوية في المالية، ولابد من ذرع الأرض وتقويم البناء تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٠٠/٨]
ويفرز كل نصيب أي يميز كل نصيب بطريقه وشربه؛ لأن القسمة لتكميل المنفعة، وبه يكمل؛ لأنه إذا لم يفرز يبقى نصيب بعضهم متعلقا بنصيب الآخر، فلم يحصل الانفصال من كل وجه، وهذا بيان الأفضل، فإذا لم يفرزه، أو لم يمكن جاز. تكملة البحر الرائق: ۳۰۰/۸] قال في "الفتح" بعد ما نقل من "الزيلعي" وغيره: كون الإفراز أفضل، وفيه تأمل مع ما سيأتي من قولهم وإن قسم ولأحدهم مسيل أو طريق في ملك الآخر صرف عنه إن أمكن وإلا فسخت. واعلم أن في طريق الدور والأرض يكفي مرور رجل وثور ولا يشترط مرور الحمولة والعجل، كذا في القهستاني. (تكملة، فتح الأنصباء بالأول إلخ يعني يسمي القاسم الأنصباء بالأول والثاني والثالث من طرف شاء، مثلا إذا جعل الجانب الغربي أولا يجعل ما يليه ثانيا، ثم ما يليه ثالثا إلى الآخر. (ملا مسكين) ويكتب أساميهم أي يكتب أسامي الشركاء ويقرع بينهم، فمن خرج اسمه أولا، فله السهم الأول، ومن خرج اسمه ثانيا، فله السهم الثاني، والقرعة لتطييب قلوبهم، فلو أقسم الإمام بلا قرعة جاز؛ لأنه في معنى القضاء، فيملك الإلزام.
وكيفية القرعة: أن ينظر إلى أقل الأنصباء، فيقدر به آخر السهام حتى إذا كان العقار بين ثلاثة، لأحدهم النصف وللآخر الثلث وللآخر السدس، جعلها أسداسا؛ لأنه أقل الأنصباء، فيكتب أسماء الشركاء في بطاقات وتطوى كل بطاقة، ويجعلها شبه البندقة ويدخلها في طين، ثم يخرجها حتى إذا انشقت يدلكها، ثم يجعلها في كمه أو وعاء، فيخرجها واحدا بعد واحد فمن خرج اسمه أولا، فله السهم الأول، ومن خرج ثانيا، فله السهم الثاني، ومن خرج ثالثا، فله السهم الثالث إلى أن : ينتهي إلى الأخير، فإن خرج أولا في المثال الذي ذكرناه اسم صاحب =
Book of Division. Issues of Division. And goods of one type are divided, but two types, jewels, slaves, pigeons, a well and a millstone are divided compulsorily only with their consent. Shared houses, or a house and a garden, or a house and a shop, each is divided between two or more. 'And goods of one type are divided' etc.: i.e., goods are divided compulsorily if they are of one type because consideration of exchange in financial benefit is possible when the type is united due to unity of purpose, so it falls as demarcation, so the judge has the power to compel it. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:298) 'And two types are not divided' etc.: i.e., two types, jewels, and what is conjuncted to them of slaves, pigeons, well, and millstone are not divided except with the consent of the partners. So his saying 'except with their consent' relates to all, meaning the judge cannot compel division of two types by dividing different types, e.g., putting the share of one in camels and the other in cows, because that entails loss of the type of benefit for the one who refuses, since before division he had benefit in both types, and after division the benefit of one is lost, so the division is not demarcation but exchange, which is not permissible except by mutual consent. (marginal note: jama' 'adam?) If it is said: a condition for the validity of division is that one benefit from the divided thing as before division? I say: that is a condition for compulsion, not a condition for division by mutual consent. Similarly, jewels are not divided compulsorily due to excessive disparity, and because ignorance of jewels is greater than ignorance of slaves, hence if one marries for a pearl or a ruby, or divorces for them, the dower is not valid, but if one marries or divorces for a slave it is valid, so it is more appropriate that one is not compelled to division. It is said: large ones are not divided due to excessive disparity, but small ones are divided due to little disparity. It is said: if their types differ they are not divided; if they are uniform they are divided like other types. (Fath, Takmila with clarification and abridgment) 'And slaves': i.e., slaves are also not divided without mutual consent according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is permissible because of unity of type, so they become like camels, horses, and sheep, and the three (imams) said so. For him (Abu Hanifa): division of slaves is difficult due to their internal qualities which are not known, and equalization is not possible, so it is not divided except by mutual consent. This difference is when the slaves are alone and there is no other type of goods with them, and they are only males or only females. But if they are mixed between males and females, it is not divided by consensus. If there is something else with the slaves that can be divided, division of slaves is permissible as a subsidiary to others by consensus. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:349) 'And pigeons' etc.: i.e., these three are not divided except with their consent due to the harm caused to all. If the partners themselves divide the pigeon coop or well, it is permissible, and each has a type of benefit, e.g., making his share of the pigeon coop a room. If they both request division from the judge, does he divide? There are two narrations: in one, he does not divide because it entails loss of benefit, and the judge does not have that because it would be foolishness; in another, he divides because they consented to that, and the book (Kanz) pointed to that because there is some benefit. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:299) 'Except with their consent': relates to the six issues mentioned from his saying 'And not divide'. 'Shared houses' etc.: i.e., if there are shared houses between two or more, or a house and a garden, or a house and a shop that are shared, each of the houses, or the house and garden, or the house and shop are divided separately, and not as a single division. As for shared houses: the mentioned is the statement of Abu Hanifa. If two men have houses or two houses in one city, even if adjacent, he said: i.e., he equalizes them according to shares of division because financial value is known by valuation separately. And the divider (qasim) describes what he divides, adjusts, measures, evaluates the building, and separates each share with its pathway and waterway, and labels the shares as first, second, third, and writes their names (gathering share and fourth, etc.) (names of partners) even if they are in different districts or two districts and they request the judge to divide them, then he divides each house separately, and does not divide them as one division except with their mutual consent. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: if he sees the division as more beneficial, he may divide some into others because they are of one type, so they become like two rooms in one house. For him (Abu Hanifa): they differ greatly in location and neighbors, and division is based on equality. On this difference are shared lands. Houses in two cities are not divided by consensus according to what Hilal narrated, and from Muhammad that they are divided. As for a house and a garden or a house and a shop, due to difference of type, riba is feared. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:349) 'And the divider describes': i.e., writes on a paper so he can remember it. He said in al-'Inayah: he writes that the share of so-and-so is such, and so-and-so such, if they want to submit that paper to the judge to conduct the lottery himself. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:300) 'And measures': because the area is known by measurement, and financial value by valuation, and it is necessary to know them to enable equalization in value, and measurement of land and valuation of building are necessary. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:300) 'And separates each share': i.e., distinguishes each share with its pathway and waterway because division is to complete benefit, and by that it is complete; because if he does not separate, the share of some remains connected to the share of others, so separation is not achieved in every aspect. This is a statement of the best, so if he does not separate it, or cannot, it is permissible. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:300) He said in al-Fath after quoting from al-Zayla'i and others: that separation is best is a consideration along with what will come of their saying: if he divided and one has a water channel or pathway in the property of another, it is diverted if possible, otherwise the division is annulled. Know that in the pathway of houses and land, the passage of a man and an ox suffices, and the passage of a loaded animal and a cart is not required. (Takmila, Fath 'Labels shares with first' etc.: i.e., the divider names the shares as first, second, third from whichever side he wishes, for example if he makes the western side first, he makes what follows it second, then what follows it third, to the end. (Mulla Miskin) 'And writes their names': i.e., writes the names of the partners and draws lots among them. Whose name comes out first gets the first share, whose name comes out second gets the second share. Lottery is to please their hearts, so if the imam divides without lottery it is permissible because it is in the meaning of judgment, so he has the power to bind. The method of lottery: he looks at the smallest share and makes it the basis of the last share. For example, if the property is among three, one has half, another a third, and another a sixth, he makes them sixths (because the smallest share is one-sixth). He writes the names of the partners on tickets, folds each ticket, makes them like clay balls, puts them in clay, then takes them out, and when they split he rolls them, then puts them in his sleeve or a vessel, then takes them out one by one. Whose name comes out first gets the first share, second gets the second, third gets the third, until the last. If in our example the name of the owner of the half comes out first, he gets the first share, etc. (text ends abruptly: 'the name of the owner of the =')
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq with its commentary from Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and other sources explains the rulings on division (qismah) of jointly owned property. The passage type is a legal exposition (sharh) of the matn. The key principle is that compulsory division by the judge is only permissible when it constitutes pure demarcation (tamyiz) without converting the nature of benefit. Goods of the same type (jins) can be divided compulsorily because the benefit is uniform and exchange is possible without loss. Different types cannot be divided compulsorily because doing so would exchange one type of benefit for another (e.g., giving camels to one and cows to another) which is a transaction (mu'awadah) requiring consent. Jewels, slaves, pigeons, wells, and millstones require consent due to hidden qualities or harm. For slaves, Abu Hanifa holds that internal differences prevent compulsory division, while the two Sahibayn allow it by analogy to livestock. The commentary notes consensus when slaves are mixed gender or when slaves accompany other divisible goods. For multiple properties (houses, gardens, shops), the Hanafi rule is to divide each separately unless all parties agree to combine; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow combining if beneficial. The procedure for the divider (qasim) involves drawing a plan, measuring land, evaluating buildings, separating pathways and water rights, labeling shares, and conducting a lottery (qur'ah) to assign shares. The lottery method involves writing names on tickets, rolling them, drawing them from a vessel; the first drawn gets the first share, etc. The purpose of lottery is to satisfy the parties, but the judge may assign without lottery. The passage emphasizes that division must preserve each partner's benefit and equalize value; if separation of shares is not possible, the division may be annulled.

Key Terms
قسمة (qismah): Division of jointly owned property into separate shares, either by mutual consent or compulsorily by the judge.
عروض (urud): Goods or chattels other than real estate, including livestock, merchandise, etc.
جبرا (jabran): Compulsorily; the judge has the power to force division upon unwilling partners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the condition for compulsory division of goods?
A) They are of different types
B) They are of the same type
C) They are jewels
D) They are slaves

Key Takeaway
The judge may compel division only when goods are of the same type, turning division into pure demarcation; otherwise, it is exchange requiring mutual consent.

intermediate

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Compulsory Division of Slaves
Detailed ruling on slaves with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and consensus exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on compulsory division of slaves and evaluate the arguments of Abu Hanifa against the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Slaves' hidden internal qualities make equal division impossible, so Abu Hanifa says no compulsion; the two companions analogize to livestock.

The division of slaves (raqiq) triggers a notable ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school itself. While the Sahibayn see slaves as analogous to livestock of the same type, Abu Hanifa emphasizes the hidden qualities (ma'ani batinah) that make equalization impossible. This lesson dissects that dispute and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
The issue is whether a judge can compel division of slaves between co-owners without their consent.
The general rule for goods of same type allows compulsion, but slaves are exceptional.
2
Present Abu Hanifa's position and dalil
Abu Hanifa holds that slaves cannot be divided compulsorily because they have hidden internal qualities (ma'ani batinah) that are unknowable, making equalization (ta'dil) impossible.
Dalil: أن قسمة الرقيق متعذر لمعانيها الباطنة ولا وقوف عليها، ولا يمكن التعديل
3
Present the Sahibayn's position and dalil
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that slaves can be divided compulsorily because they are of the same type (jins), so the division is like demarcation, analogous to camels, horses, and sheep.
Dalil: بالاتحاد الجنس، فصار كالإبل والخيل والغنم
4
Note the points of consensus
The ikhtilaf exists only when slaves are alone and of the same gender. If they are mixed gender, or if they come with other divisible goods, division is not compulsory by consensus.
Mixed gender: لا يقسم بالإجماع; slaves with other goods: تبعا لغيرهم بالإجماع
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's (not compulsory), as the commentary leans toward it and it is more cautious regarding hidden defects.
Tarjih by the Takmila: the commentary sides with Abu Hanifa.

كتاب القسمة
مسائل القسمة
ويقسم العروض من جنس واحد ولا يقسم الجنسان والجواهر والرقيق والحمام جبرا والبئر والرحى إلا برضائهم . دُور مشتركة أو دار وضيعة أو دار وحانوت قسم كل بين اثنين أو أكثر
ويقسم العروض إلخ : أي يقسم العروض إذا كانت من جنس واحد جبرا؛ لأن اعتبار المبادلة في المنفعة المالية ممكن عند اتحاد الجنس؛ لاتحاد المقصود فيه، فيقع تمييزا، فيملك القاضي الإجبار عليها تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٩٨/٨] ولا يقسم إلخ: أي لا يقسم الجنسان والجواهر وما عطف عليهما من الرقيق والحمام والبئر والرحى إلا برضاء الشركاء، فقوله: "إلا "برضائهم" متعلق بالجميع يعني لا يملك القاضي الإجبار على قسمة الجنسين بأن يقسم الأجناس المختلفة قسمة بأن يجمع نصيب أحدهم في الإبل والآخر في البقر ؛ لما في ذلك من تفويت جنس المنفعة على الآبي؛ لأن قبل القسمة كان له المنفعة في الجنسين جميعا، وبعد القسمة فات منفعة أحدهما، فلم تقع القسمة تمييزا بل معاوضة، وهي لا تجوز إلا بالتراضي.
جمع
عدم
فإن قيل: شرط صحة القسمة أن ينتفع بالمقسوم كما كان قبل القسمة؟ قلت: ذاك شرط الجبر عليها لا شرط القسمة بالتراضي، وكذا لا يقسم الجواهر جبرا؛ لفحش التفاوت، ولأن جهالة الجواهر أفحش من جهالة الرقيق، ولهذا لو تزوج على لؤلؤة أو ياقوتة، أو خالع عليها لا تصح التسمية، ولو تزوج أو خالع على عبد يصح، فأولى أن لا يجبر على القسمة، وقيل: لا يقسم الكبار منها؛ لفحش التفاوت ويقسم الصغار؛ لقلة التفاوت، وقيل: إن اختلف جنسهما لا يقسم، وإن اتحد يقسم كسائر الأجناس. (فتح، تكملة بتوضيح واختصار) والرقيق: أي لا يقسم الرقيق أيضا من غير تراض عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يجوز؛ لاتحاد الجنس، فصار كالإبل والخيل والغنم، وبه قالت الثلاثة، وله: أن قسمة الرقيق متعذر لمعانيها الباطنة ولا وقوف عليها، ولا يمكن التعديل، فلا يقسم إلا بتراض، وهذا الخلاف فيما إذا كان الرقيق وحدهم وليس معهم شيء آخر من العروض، وهم ذكور فقط، أو إناث فقط، وأما إذا كانوا مختلطين بين الذكور والإناث لا يقسم بالإجماع، وإن كان مع الرقيق شيء آخر مما يقسم، جازت القسمة في الرقيق تبعا لغيرهم بالإجماع. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٤٩/٢] والحمام إلخ أي لا تقسم هذه الثلاثة إلا برضائهم لما ذكر من إلحاق الضرر بالكل، ولو اقتسما الحمام أو البئر بأنفسهم جاز، ولكل واحد نوع منفعة بأن يتخذ نصيبه من الحمام بيتا وإن طلبا جميعا القسمة من القاضي هل يقسم؟ فيه روايتان في رواية لا يقسم؛ لأنها تضمنت تفويت منفعة، وليس للقاضي ذلك؛ لأنه يكون سفها يمكنه، وفي رواية: يقسم؛ لأنهم رضوا بذلك، وإليه أشار في الكتاب؛ لأنه فيه نوع منفعة كذا في "المحيط". تكملة البحر الرائق: ۲۹۹/۸] إلا برضائهم : متعلق بالمسائل الست المذكورة من قوله: "ولا يقسم". دور مشتركة إلخ : أي إذا كانت دور مشتركة بين اثنين أو أكثر، أو دار وضيعة أو دار وحانوت مشتركة، قسم كل واحد من الدور أو من الدار والضيعة أو من الدار والحانوت على حدة، ولا تقسم قسمة واحدة، أما الدور المشتركة: فالمذكور قول أبي حنيفة، فإنه إذا كان لرجلين دور أو داران في مصر واحد، ولو كانت متلازقة - قال: أي يسويه على سهام القسمة لأن المالية تعرف بالتقويم على حدة، ويصور القاسم ما يقسمه ويعدّله ويذرعه ويقوم البناء، ويفرز كل ولا تقسم قسمة واحدة نصيب بطريقه وشربه ويلقب الأنصباء بالأول والثاني والثالث، ويكتب أساميهم = جمع نصيب والرابع وهلم جرا أسامي الشركاء أو متباينة في محلة أو محلتين وطلبا من القاضي قسمتهما، فإنه يقسم كل دار على حدة، ولا يقسمها قسمة واحدة إلا بتراضيهما. وقالا: إن رأى القسمة أصلح يقسم بعضها في بعض؛ لأنها من جنس واحد، فصار كبيتين في دار واحدة، وله: أنها تتفاوت بالمكان والجيران تفاوتا فاحشا ومبناها على التساوي، وعلى هذا الخلاف الأراضي المشتركة والدور في مصرين لا تقسم بالإجماع فيما رواه هلال وعن محمد أنها تقسم، وأما الدار والضيعة أو الدار والحانوت، فلاختلاف الجنس فيتوهم فيه الربا رمز الحقائق: ٣٤٩/٢]
ويصور القاسم: أي يكتب على قرطاس؛ ليمكنه حفظه، قال في "العناية": يكتب أن نصيب فلان كذا، وفلان كذا إن أرادوا رفع تلك الكاغذة إلى القاضي؛ ليتولى الإقراع بينهم بنفسه. [ تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٠٠/٨] ويذرعه: لأن قدر الساحة يعرف بالذرع، والمالية بالتقويم، ولابد من معرفتها؛ ليمكنه التسوية في المالية، ولابد من ذرع الأرض وتقويم البناء تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٠٠/٨]
ويفرز كل نصيب أي يميز كل نصيب بطريقه وشربه؛ لأن القسمة لتكميل المنفعة، وبه يكمل؛ لأنه إذا لم يفرز يبقى نصيب بعضهم متعلقا بنصيب الآخر، فلم يحصل الانفصال من كل وجه، وهذا بيان الأفضل، فإذا لم يفرزه، أو لم يمكن جاز. تكملة البحر الرائق: ۳۰۰/۸] قال في "الفتح" بعد ما نقل من "الزيلعي" وغيره: كون الإفراز أفضل، وفيه تأمل مع ما سيأتي من قولهم وإن قسم ولأحدهم مسيل أو طريق في ملك الآخر صرف عنه إن أمكن وإلا فسخت. واعلم أن في طريق الدور والأرض يكفي مرور رجل وثور ولا يشترط مرور الحمولة والعجل، كذا في القهستاني. (تكملة، فتح الأنصباء بالأول إلخ يعني يسمي القاسم الأنصباء بالأول والثاني والثالث من طرف شاء، مثلا إذا جعل الجانب الغربي أولا يجعل ما يليه ثانيا، ثم ما يليه ثالثا إلى الآخر. (ملا مسكين) ويكتب أساميهم أي يكتب أسامي الشركاء ويقرع بينهم، فمن خرج اسمه أولا، فله السهم الأول، ومن خرج اسمه ثانيا، فله السهم الثاني، والقرعة لتطييب قلوبهم، فلو أقسم الإمام بلا قرعة جاز؛ لأنه في معنى القضاء، فيملك الإلزام.
وكيفية القرعة: أن ينظر إلى أقل الأنصباء، فيقدر به آخر السهام حتى إذا كان العقار بين ثلاثة، لأحدهم النصف وللآخر الثلث وللآخر السدس، جعلها أسداسا؛ لأنه أقل الأنصباء، فيكتب أسماء الشركاء في بطاقات وتطوى كل بطاقة، ويجعلها شبه البندقة ويدخلها في طين، ثم يخرجها حتى إذا انشقت يدلكها، ثم يجعلها في كمه أو وعاء، فيخرجها واحدا بعد واحد فمن خرج اسمه أولا، فله السهم الأول، ومن خرج ثانيا، فله السهم الثاني، ومن خرج ثالثا، فله السهم الثالث إلى أن : ينتهي إلى الأخير، فإن خرج أولا في المثال الذي ذكرناه اسم صاحب =
Book of Division. Issues of Division. And goods of one type are divided, but two types, jewels, slaves, pigeons, a well and a millstone are divided compulsorily only with their consent. Shared houses, or a house and a garden, or a house and a shop, each is divided between two or more. 'And goods of one type are divided' etc.: i.e., goods are divided compulsorily if they are of one type because consideration of exchange in financial benefit is possible when the type is united due to unity of purpose, so it falls as demarcation, so the judge has the power to compel it. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:298) 'And two types are not divided' etc.: i.e., two types, jewels, and what is conjuncted to them of slaves, pigeons, well, and millstone are not divided except with the consent of the partners. So his saying 'except with their consent' relates to all, meaning the judge cannot compel division of two types by dividing different types, e.g., putting the share of one in camels and the other in cows, because that entails loss of the type of benefit for the one who refuses, since before division he had benefit in both types, and after division the benefit of one is lost, so the division is not demarcation but exchange, which is not permissible except by mutual consent. (marginal note: jama' 'adam?) If it is said: a condition for the validity of division is that one benefit from the divided thing as before division? I say: that is a condition for compulsion, not a condition for division by mutual consent. Similarly, jewels are not divided compulsorily due to excessive disparity, and because ignorance of jewels is greater than ignorance of slaves, hence if one marries for a pearl or a ruby, or divorces for them, the dower is not valid, but if one marries or divorces for a slave it is valid, so it is more appropriate that one is not compelled to division. It is said: large ones are not divided due to excessive disparity, but small ones are divided due to little disparity. It is said: if their types differ they are not divided; if they are uniform they are divided like other types. (Fath, Takmila with clarification and abridgment) 'And slaves': i.e., slaves are also not divided without mutual consent according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is permissible because of unity of type, so they become like camels, horses, and sheep, and the three (imams) said so. For him (Abu Hanifa): division of slaves is difficult due to their internal qualities which are not known, and equalization is not possible, so it is not divided except by mutual consent. This difference is when the slaves are alone and there is no other type of goods with them, and they are only males or only females. But if they are mixed between males and females, it is not divided by consensus. If there is something else with the slaves that can be divided, division of slaves is permissible as a subsidiary to others by consensus. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:349) 'And pigeons' etc.: i.e., these three are not divided except with their consent due to the harm caused to all. If the partners themselves divide the pigeon coop or well, it is permissible, and each has a type of benefit, e.g., making his share of the pigeon coop a room. If they both request division from the judge, does he divide? There are two narrations: in one, he does not divide because it entails loss of benefit, and the judge does not have that because it would be foolishness; in another, he divides because they consented to that, and the book (Kanz) pointed to that because there is some benefit. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:299) 'Except with their consent': relates to the six issues mentioned from his saying 'And not divide'. 'Shared houses' etc.: i.e., if there are shared houses between two or more, or a house and a garden, or a house and a shop that are shared, each of the houses, or the house and garden, or the house and shop are divided separately, and not as a single division. As for shared houses: the mentioned is the statement of Abu Hanifa. If two men have houses or two houses in one city, even if adjacent, he said: i.e., he equalizes them according to shares of division because financial value is known by valuation separately. And the divider (qasim) describes what he divides, adjusts, measures, evaluates the building, and separates each share with its pathway and waterway, and labels the shares as first, second, third, and writes their names (gathering share and fourth, etc.) (names of partners) even if they are in different districts or two districts and they request the judge to divide them, then he divides each house separately, and does not divide them as one division except with their mutual consent. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: if he sees the division as more beneficial, he may divide some into others because they are of one type, so they become like two rooms in one house. For him (Abu Hanifa): they differ greatly in location and neighbors, and division is based on equality. On this difference are shared lands. Houses in two cities are not divided by consensus according to what Hilal narrated, and from Muhammad that they are divided. As for a house and a garden or a house and a shop, due to difference of type, riba is feared. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:349) 'And the divider describes': i.e., writes on a paper so he can remember it. He said in al-'Inayah: he writes that the share of so-and-so is such, and so-and-so such, if they want to submit that paper to the judge to conduct the lottery himself. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:300) 'And measures': because the area is known by measurement, and financial value by valuation, and it is necessary to know them to enable equalization in value, and measurement of land and valuation of building are necessary. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:300) 'And separates each share': i.e., distinguishes each share with its pathway and waterway because division is to complete benefit, and by that it is complete; because if he does not separate, the share of some remains connected to the share of others, so separation is not achieved in every aspect. This is a statement of the best, so if he does not separate it, or cannot, it is permissible. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:300) He said in al-Fath after quoting from al-Zayla'i and others: that separation is best is a consideration along with what will come of their saying: if he divided and one has a water channel or pathway in the property of another, it is diverted if possible, otherwise the division is annulled. Know that in the pathway of houses and land, the passage of a man and an ox suffices, and the passage of a loaded animal and a cart is not required. (Takmila, Fath 'Labels shares with first' etc.: i.e., the divider names the shares as first, second, third from whichever side he wishes, for example if he makes the western side first, he makes what follows it second, then what follows it third, to the end. (Mulla Miskin) 'And writes their names': i.e., writes the names of the partners and draws lots among them. Whose name comes out first gets the first share, whose name comes out second gets the second share. Lottery is to please their hearts, so if the imam divides without lottery it is permissible because it is in the meaning of judgment, so he has the power to bind. The method of lottery: he looks at the smallest share and makes it the basis of the last share. For example, if the property is among three, one has half, another a third, and another a sixth, he makes them sixths (because the smallest share is one-sixth). He writes the names of the partners on tickets, folds each ticket, makes them like clay balls, puts them in clay, then takes them out, and when they split he rolls them, then puts them in his sleeve or a vessel, then takes them out one by one. Whose name comes out first gets the first share, second gets the second, third gets the third, until the last. If in our example the name of the owner of the half comes out first, he gets the first share, etc. (text ends abruptly: 'the name of the owner of the =')
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq with its commentary from Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and other sources explains the rulings on division (qismah) of jointly owned property. The passage type is a legal exposition (sharh) of the matn. The key principle is that compulsory division by the judge is only permissible when it constitutes pure demarcation (tamyiz) without converting the nature of benefit. Goods of the same type (jins) can be divided compulsorily because the benefit is uniform and exchange is possible without loss. Different types cannot be divided compulsorily because doing so would exchange one type of benefit for another (e.g., giving camels to one and cows to another) which is a transaction (mu'awadah) requiring consent. Jewels, slaves, pigeons, wells, and millstones require consent due to hidden qualities or harm. For slaves, Abu Hanifa holds that internal differences prevent compulsory division, while the two Sahibayn allow it by analogy to livestock. The commentary notes consensus when slaves are mixed gender or when slaves accompany other divisible goods. For multiple properties (houses, gardens, shops), the Hanafi rule is to divide each separately unless all parties agree to combine; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow combining if beneficial. The procedure for the divider (qasim) involves drawing a plan, measuring land, evaluating buildings, separating pathways and water rights, labeling shares, and conducting a lottery (qur'ah) to assign shares. The lottery method involves writing names on tickets, rolling them, drawing them from a vessel; the first drawn gets the first share, etc. The purpose of lottery is to satisfy the parties, but the judge may assign without lottery. The passage emphasizes that division must preserve each partner's benefit and equalize value; if separation of shares is not possible, the division may be annulled.

Key Terms
رقيق (raqiq): Slaves; human beings owned as property.
معان باطنة (ma'ani batinah): Hidden internal qualities or characteristics, such as health, temperament, skills, etc., which are not readily apparent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, can the judge compel division of slaves?
A) Yes, because slaves are of the same type.
B) No, because slaves have hidden qualities that prevent equalization.
C) Yes, but only if the slaves are male.
D) No, because slaves are human beings.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's authoritative position is that slaves cannot be divided compulsorily due to unknowable hidden qualities, contrasting with the analogical reasoning of the two companions.

intermediate

Division of Multiple Properties and Procedural Steps
Procedural rules for dividing multiple properties and the detailed steps of the divider.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how multiple shared properties are divided separately and describe the divider's procedural steps: description, measurement, valuation, separation, and lottery.

Core Idea
Each shared property must be divided separately; the divider measures, values, and assigns shares by lottery to ensure fairness and avoid prejudice.

When co-owners have multiple distinct properties (houses, gardens, shops), the Hanafi rule is to divide each property separately unless all agree to combine. This lesson covers the procedure for the divider (qasim) including drawing a plan, measuring land, evaluating buildings, assigning pathways, and conducting a lottery to allocate shares. The goal is to achieve a division that preserves each partner's benefit.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle: separate division of each property
If there are multiple shared properties (e.g., two houses, or a house and a garden), each is divided separately. The judge cannot lump them into one division without consent.
Abu Hanifa's view: separate division; Sahibayn may combine if beneficial.
2
The role of the divider (qasim)
The divider describes the property (yusawwir), measures the land (yadhr'u), values the building, and separates each share with its pathway and waterway.
ويصور القاسم: يكتب على قرطاس; ويذرعه; ويفرز كل نصيب
3
Separation of rights: pathways and water
Each share must be assigned its own access route and water rights. Without separation, the division is incomplete; if separation is impossible, the division may be annulled.
ويفرز كل نصيب بطريقه وشربه
4
Labeling shares and lottery
The divider labels shares as first, second, third, etc., writes the partners' names on tickets, and draws lots. The first drawn receives the first share, etc.
القرعة لتطييب قلوبهم
5
Details of the lottery procedure
The divider looks at the smallest share to determine the number of lots, writes names on tickets, rolls them, and draws one by one. The order of drawing determines the assignment of labeled shares.
يقدر به آخر السهام; يكتب أسماء الشركاء في بطاقات ويخرجها واحد بعد واحد

كتاب القسمة
مسائل القسمة
ويقسم العروض من جنس واحد ولا يقسم الجنسان والجواهر والرقيق والحمام جبرا والبئر والرحى إلا برضائهم . دُور مشتركة أو دار وضيعة أو دار وحانوت قسم كل بين اثنين أو أكثر
ويقسم العروض إلخ : أي يقسم العروض إذا كانت من جنس واحد جبرا؛ لأن اعتبار المبادلة في المنفعة المالية ممكن عند اتحاد الجنس؛ لاتحاد المقصود فيه، فيقع تمييزا، فيملك القاضي الإجبار عليها تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٩٨/٨] ولا يقسم إلخ: أي لا يقسم الجنسان والجواهر وما عطف عليهما من الرقيق والحمام والبئر والرحى إلا برضاء الشركاء، فقوله: "إلا "برضائهم" متعلق بالجميع يعني لا يملك القاضي الإجبار على قسمة الجنسين بأن يقسم الأجناس المختلفة قسمة بأن يجمع نصيب أحدهم في الإبل والآخر في البقر ؛ لما في ذلك من تفويت جنس المنفعة على الآبي؛ لأن قبل القسمة كان له المنفعة في الجنسين جميعا، وبعد القسمة فات منفعة أحدهما، فلم تقع القسمة تمييزا بل معاوضة، وهي لا تجوز إلا بالتراضي.
جمع
عدم
فإن قيل: شرط صحة القسمة أن ينتفع بالمقسوم كما كان قبل القسمة؟ قلت: ذاك شرط الجبر عليها لا شرط القسمة بالتراضي، وكذا لا يقسم الجواهر جبرا؛ لفحش التفاوت، ولأن جهالة الجواهر أفحش من جهالة الرقيق، ولهذا لو تزوج على لؤلؤة أو ياقوتة، أو خالع عليها لا تصح التسمية، ولو تزوج أو خالع على عبد يصح، فأولى أن لا يجبر على القسمة، وقيل: لا يقسم الكبار منها؛ لفحش التفاوت ويقسم الصغار؛ لقلة التفاوت، وقيل: إن اختلف جنسهما لا يقسم، وإن اتحد يقسم كسائر الأجناس. (فتح، تكملة بتوضيح واختصار) والرقيق: أي لا يقسم الرقيق أيضا من غير تراض عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يجوز؛ لاتحاد الجنس، فصار كالإبل والخيل والغنم، وبه قالت الثلاثة، وله: أن قسمة الرقيق متعذر لمعانيها الباطنة ولا وقوف عليها، ولا يمكن التعديل، فلا يقسم إلا بتراض، وهذا الخلاف فيما إذا كان الرقيق وحدهم وليس معهم شيء آخر من العروض، وهم ذكور فقط، أو إناث فقط، وأما إذا كانوا مختلطين بين الذكور والإناث لا يقسم بالإجماع، وإن كان مع الرقيق شيء آخر مما يقسم، جازت القسمة في الرقيق تبعا لغيرهم بالإجماع. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٤٩/٢] والحمام إلخ أي لا تقسم هذه الثلاثة إلا برضائهم لما ذكر من إلحاق الضرر بالكل، ولو اقتسما الحمام أو البئر بأنفسهم جاز، ولكل واحد نوع منفعة بأن يتخذ نصيبه من الحمام بيتا وإن طلبا جميعا القسمة من القاضي هل يقسم؟ فيه روايتان في رواية لا يقسم؛ لأنها تضمنت تفويت منفعة، وليس للقاضي ذلك؛ لأنه يكون سفها يمكنه، وفي رواية: يقسم؛ لأنهم رضوا بذلك، وإليه أشار في الكتاب؛ لأنه فيه نوع منفعة كذا في "المحيط". تكملة البحر الرائق: ۲۹۹/۸] إلا برضائهم : متعلق بالمسائل الست المذكورة من قوله: "ولا يقسم". دور مشتركة إلخ : أي إذا كانت دور مشتركة بين اثنين أو أكثر، أو دار وضيعة أو دار وحانوت مشتركة، قسم كل واحد من الدور أو من الدار والضيعة أو من الدار والحانوت على حدة، ولا تقسم قسمة واحدة، أما الدور المشتركة: فالمذكور قول أبي حنيفة، فإنه إذا كان لرجلين دور أو داران في مصر واحد، ولو كانت متلازقة - قال: أي يسويه على سهام القسمة لأن المالية تعرف بالتقويم على حدة، ويصور القاسم ما يقسمه ويعدّله ويذرعه ويقوم البناء، ويفرز كل ولا تقسم قسمة واحدة نصيب بطريقه وشربه ويلقب الأنصباء بالأول والثاني والثالث، ويكتب أساميهم = جمع نصيب والرابع وهلم جرا أسامي الشركاء أو متباينة في محلة أو محلتين وطلبا من القاضي قسمتهما، فإنه يقسم كل دار على حدة، ولا يقسمها قسمة واحدة إلا بتراضيهما. وقالا: إن رأى القسمة أصلح يقسم بعضها في بعض؛ لأنها من جنس واحد، فصار كبيتين في دار واحدة، وله: أنها تتفاوت بالمكان والجيران تفاوتا فاحشا ومبناها على التساوي، وعلى هذا الخلاف الأراضي المشتركة والدور في مصرين لا تقسم بالإجماع فيما رواه هلال وعن محمد أنها تقسم، وأما الدار والضيعة أو الدار والحانوت، فلاختلاف الجنس فيتوهم فيه الربا رمز الحقائق: ٣٤٩/٢]
ويصور القاسم: أي يكتب على قرطاس؛ ليمكنه حفظه، قال في "العناية": يكتب أن نصيب فلان كذا، وفلان كذا إن أرادوا رفع تلك الكاغذة إلى القاضي؛ ليتولى الإقراع بينهم بنفسه. [ تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٠٠/٨] ويذرعه: لأن قدر الساحة يعرف بالذرع، والمالية بالتقويم، ولابد من معرفتها؛ ليمكنه التسوية في المالية، ولابد من ذرع الأرض وتقويم البناء تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٠٠/٨]
ويفرز كل نصيب أي يميز كل نصيب بطريقه وشربه؛ لأن القسمة لتكميل المنفعة، وبه يكمل؛ لأنه إذا لم يفرز يبقى نصيب بعضهم متعلقا بنصيب الآخر، فلم يحصل الانفصال من كل وجه، وهذا بيان الأفضل، فإذا لم يفرزه، أو لم يمكن جاز. تكملة البحر الرائق: ۳۰۰/۸] قال في "الفتح" بعد ما نقل من "الزيلعي" وغيره: كون الإفراز أفضل، وفيه تأمل مع ما سيأتي من قولهم وإن قسم ولأحدهم مسيل أو طريق في ملك الآخر صرف عنه إن أمكن وإلا فسخت. واعلم أن في طريق الدور والأرض يكفي مرور رجل وثور ولا يشترط مرور الحمولة والعجل، كذا في القهستاني. (تكملة، فتح الأنصباء بالأول إلخ يعني يسمي القاسم الأنصباء بالأول والثاني والثالث من طرف شاء، مثلا إذا جعل الجانب الغربي أولا يجعل ما يليه ثانيا، ثم ما يليه ثالثا إلى الآخر. (ملا مسكين) ويكتب أساميهم أي يكتب أسامي الشركاء ويقرع بينهم، فمن خرج اسمه أولا، فله السهم الأول، ومن خرج اسمه ثانيا، فله السهم الثاني، والقرعة لتطييب قلوبهم، فلو أقسم الإمام بلا قرعة جاز؛ لأنه في معنى القضاء، فيملك الإلزام.
وكيفية القرعة: أن ينظر إلى أقل الأنصباء، فيقدر به آخر السهام حتى إذا كان العقار بين ثلاثة، لأحدهم النصف وللآخر الثلث وللآخر السدس، جعلها أسداسا؛ لأنه أقل الأنصباء، فيكتب أسماء الشركاء في بطاقات وتطوى كل بطاقة، ويجعلها شبه البندقة ويدخلها في طين، ثم يخرجها حتى إذا انشقت يدلكها، ثم يجعلها في كمه أو وعاء، فيخرجها واحدا بعد واحد فمن خرج اسمه أولا، فله السهم الأول، ومن خرج ثانيا، فله السهم الثاني، ومن خرج ثالثا، فله السهم الثالث إلى أن : ينتهي إلى الأخير، فإن خرج أولا في المثال الذي ذكرناه اسم صاحب =
Book of Division. Issues of Division. And goods of one type are divided, but two types, jewels, slaves, pigeons, a well and a millstone are divided compulsorily only with their consent. Shared houses, or a house and a garden, or a house and a shop, each is divided between two or more. 'And goods of one type are divided' etc.: i.e., goods are divided compulsorily if they are of one type because consideration of exchange in financial benefit is possible when the type is united due to unity of purpose, so it falls as demarcation, so the judge has the power to compel it. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:298) 'And two types are not divided' etc.: i.e., two types, jewels, and what is conjuncted to them of slaves, pigeons, well, and millstone are not divided except with the consent of the partners. So his saying 'except with their consent' relates to all, meaning the judge cannot compel division of two types by dividing different types, e.g., putting the share of one in camels and the other in cows, because that entails loss of the type of benefit for the one who refuses, since before division he had benefit in both types, and after division the benefit of one is lost, so the division is not demarcation but exchange, which is not permissible except by mutual consent. (marginal note: jama' 'adam?) If it is said: a condition for the validity of division is that one benefit from the divided thing as before division? I say: that is a condition for compulsion, not a condition for division by mutual consent. Similarly, jewels are not divided compulsorily due to excessive disparity, and because ignorance of jewels is greater than ignorance of slaves, hence if one marries for a pearl or a ruby, or divorces for them, the dower is not valid, but if one marries or divorces for a slave it is valid, so it is more appropriate that one is not compelled to division. It is said: large ones are not divided due to excessive disparity, but small ones are divided due to little disparity. It is said: if their types differ they are not divided; if they are uniform they are divided like other types. (Fath, Takmila with clarification and abridgment) 'And slaves': i.e., slaves are also not divided without mutual consent according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is permissible because of unity of type, so they become like camels, horses, and sheep, and the three (imams) said so. For him (Abu Hanifa): division of slaves is difficult due to their internal qualities which are not known, and equalization is not possible, so it is not divided except by mutual consent. This difference is when the slaves are alone and there is no other type of goods with them, and they are only males or only females. But if they are mixed between males and females, it is not divided by consensus. If there is something else with the slaves that can be divided, division of slaves is permissible as a subsidiary to others by consensus. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:349) 'And pigeons' etc.: i.e., these three are not divided except with their consent due to the harm caused to all. If the partners themselves divide the pigeon coop or well, it is permissible, and each has a type of benefit, e.g., making his share of the pigeon coop a room. If they both request division from the judge, does he divide? There are two narrations: in one, he does not divide because it entails loss of benefit, and the judge does not have that because it would be foolishness; in another, he divides because they consented to that, and the book (Kanz) pointed to that because there is some benefit. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:299) 'Except with their consent': relates to the six issues mentioned from his saying 'And not divide'. 'Shared houses' etc.: i.e., if there are shared houses between two or more, or a house and a garden, or a house and a shop that are shared, each of the houses, or the house and garden, or the house and shop are divided separately, and not as a single division. As for shared houses: the mentioned is the statement of Abu Hanifa. If two men have houses or two houses in one city, even if adjacent, he said: i.e., he equalizes them according to shares of division because financial value is known by valuation separately. And the divider (qasim) describes what he divides, adjusts, measures, evaluates the building, and separates each share with its pathway and waterway, and labels the shares as first, second, third, and writes their names (gathering share and fourth, etc.) (names of partners) even if they are in different districts or two districts and they request the judge to divide them, then he divides each house separately, and does not divide them as one division except with their mutual consent. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: if he sees the division as more beneficial, he may divide some into others because they are of one type, so they become like two rooms in one house. For him (Abu Hanifa): they differ greatly in location and neighbors, and division is based on equality. On this difference are shared lands. Houses in two cities are not divided by consensus according to what Hilal narrated, and from Muhammad that they are divided. As for a house and a garden or a house and a shop, due to difference of type, riba is feared. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:349) 'And the divider describes': i.e., writes on a paper so he can remember it. He said in al-'Inayah: he writes that the share of so-and-so is such, and so-and-so such, if they want to submit that paper to the judge to conduct the lottery himself. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:300) 'And measures': because the area is known by measurement, and financial value by valuation, and it is necessary to know them to enable equalization in value, and measurement of land and valuation of building are necessary. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:300) 'And separates each share': i.e., distinguishes each share with its pathway and waterway because division is to complete benefit, and by that it is complete; because if he does not separate, the share of some remains connected to the share of others, so separation is not achieved in every aspect. This is a statement of the best, so if he does not separate it, or cannot, it is permissible. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:300) He said in al-Fath after quoting from al-Zayla'i and others: that separation is best is a consideration along with what will come of their saying: if he divided and one has a water channel or pathway in the property of another, it is diverted if possible, otherwise the division is annulled. Know that in the pathway of houses and land, the passage of a man and an ox suffices, and the passage of a loaded animal and a cart is not required. (Takmila, Fath 'Labels shares with first' etc.: i.e., the divider names the shares as first, second, third from whichever side he wishes, for example if he makes the western side first, he makes what follows it second, then what follows it third, to the end. (Mulla Miskin) 'And writes their names': i.e., writes the names of the partners and draws lots among them. Whose name comes out first gets the first share, whose name comes out second gets the second share. Lottery is to please their hearts, so if the imam divides without lottery it is permissible because it is in the meaning of judgment, so he has the power to bind. The method of lottery: he looks at the smallest share and makes it the basis of the last share. For example, if the property is among three, one has half, another a third, and another a sixth, he makes them sixths (because the smallest share is one-sixth). He writes the names of the partners on tickets, folds each ticket, makes them like clay balls, puts them in clay, then takes them out, and when they split he rolls them, then puts them in his sleeve or a vessel, then takes them out one by one. Whose name comes out first gets the first share, second gets the second, third gets the third, until the last. If in our example the name of the owner of the half comes out first, he gets the first share, etc. (text ends abruptly: 'the name of the owner of the =')
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq with its commentary from Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and other sources explains the rulings on division (qismah) of jointly owned property. The passage type is a legal exposition (sharh) of the matn. The key principle is that compulsory division by the judge is only permissible when it constitutes pure demarcation (tamyiz) without converting the nature of benefit. Goods of the same type (jins) can be divided compulsorily because the benefit is uniform and exchange is possible without loss. Different types cannot be divided compulsorily because doing so would exchange one type of benefit for another (e.g., giving camels to one and cows to another) which is a transaction (mu'awadah) requiring consent. Jewels, slaves, pigeons, wells, and millstones require consent due to hidden qualities or harm. For slaves, Abu Hanifa holds that internal differences prevent compulsory division, while the two Sahibayn allow it by analogy to livestock. The commentary notes consensus when slaves are mixed gender or when slaves accompany other divisible goods. For multiple properties (houses, gardens, shops), the Hanafi rule is to divide each separately unless all parties agree to combine; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow combining if beneficial. The procedure for the divider (qasim) involves drawing a plan, measuring land, evaluating buildings, separating pathways and water rights, labeling shares, and conducting a lottery (qur'ah) to assign shares. The lottery method involves writing names on tickets, rolling them, drawing them from a vessel; the first drawn gets the first share, etc. The purpose of lottery is to satisfy the parties, but the judge may assign without lottery. The passage emphasizes that division must preserve each partner's benefit and equalize value; if separation of shares is not possible, the division may be annulled.

Key Terms
قاسم (qasim): The divider; the person appointed to carry out the physical division of property.
تصوير (taswir): Describing the property in writing, including a sketch or plan.
ذرع (dhar'): Measurement of land area, typically in cubits or standard units.
إفراز (ifraz): Separation of each share by marking boundaries and ensuring access rights.
قرعة (qur'ah): Lottery; a method to assign shares randomly to satisfy the partners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, how should the judge divide two houses jointly owned by two partners?
A) Combine them into one division to simplify.
B) Divide each house separately unless both partners consent to combine.
C) Divide only one house and leave the other untouched.
D) Sell both houses and divide the proceeds.

Key Takeaway
Multiple properties must be divided separately; the divider must measure, value, separate access rights, and may use lottery to assign shares fairly.

Using Lottery in Division of Property
Ruling on using lottery to assign shares in division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on using lottery in property division, distinguish it from gambling (qimar), and cite the Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Lottery in division is permissible because rights preexist; it is not gambling.

When co-owners cannot agree on how to divide shared property, the Hanafi school allows casting lots as a fair method. However, some may mistakenly equate this with gambling. The text from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses this concern directly, clarifying the legal basis and distinguishing lottery from prohibited games of chance. We will unpack the ruling, its proof, and a subtle tension in the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the ruling on using lottery in division of property? The text states it is permissible and carried out to soothe hearts.
The act is mubah (permissible).
2
Understand the objection
An objector claims that tying entitlement to lottery is gambling, which is haram. Recognize the strength of this objection: uncertainty in allocation resembles qimar.
This is a typical qiyas argument.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The key distinction: entitlement (istihqaq) exists before the lottery. The lottery only determines which specific share each partner receives, not whether they get anything. Gambling creates a right where none existed.
Contrast: lottery divides preexisting rights; gambling creates new rights.
4
Examine the proof
The text cites Quranic stories of prophets Zakariyya (3:44) and Yunus (37:141) casting lots. These are evidence that lottery is legislated and not inherently prohibited.
The proof is from the Quran (dalil naqli).
5
Evaluate the tension
The passage notes a contradiction: first the author says qiyas would reject lottery and istihsan permits it, but later argues that qiyas also permits it. Reflect on how this highlights the interplay between istihsan and qiyas in Hanafi methodology.
This tension is not resolved in the text; it shows scholarly debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقرع، فمن خرج اسمه أولا، فله السهم الأول، ومن خرج ثانيا، فله الثاني، ولا يدخل لتطييب القلوب من هؤلاء. فإن قلت: تعليق الاستحقاق بالقرعة قمار وهو حرام؟ قلت: لا نسلم؛ فإن الاستحقاق كان ثابتا قبلها وإنما صير إليها؛ لتطييب قلوبهم كالقرعة بين النساء للسفر أو للبداءة في القسم، وهذا ليس بقمار، وإنما القمار اسم لما يأخذون به شيئا لم يكن لهم قبل ذلك لا مثل هذه فإنها مشروعة كما أخبر الله تعالى حكاية عن يونس وزكريا على السلالا كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذْ يُلْقُونَ أَقْلَامَهُمْ أَيُّهُمْ يَكْفُلُ﴾ (آل عمران:٤٤) الآية، وقوله تعالى: ﴿فَسَاهَمَ فَكَانَ مِنَ الْمُدْحَضِينَ﴾ (الصافات: ١٤١). ولقائل أن يقول: بين أول كلامهم وآخره تدافع؛ لأنهم صرحوا أولا بأن مشروعية استعمال القرعة هنا جواب استحسان والقياس يأبى ذلك، وقالوا آخرا: إن هذا ليس بقمار وبينوا الفرق بينه وبين القمار وذكروا له نظائر من الكتاب والسنة فقط دل على أنه لا يأباه القياس أصلا بل هو يقتضيه القياس أيضا فتدافعها.
And they cast lots; whoever's name comes out first gets the first share, and whoever comes out second gets the second, and it is only to soothe the hearts of these people. If you say: Tying entitlement to lottery is gambling and it is prohibited? I say: We do not accept; for entitlement was established before it, and it is only resorted to to soothe their hearts, like the lottery among women for travel or for beginning the division, and this is not gambling; rather gambling is a name for taking something that was not theirs before, unlike these, for it is legislated as Allah narrated about Yunus and Zakariyya, peace be upon them, as Allah said: 'And when they cast their pens [to decide] which of them would be responsible for Mary' (3:44) and His saying: 'Then he cast lots and was of the losers' (37:141). And one may say: There is contradiction between the beginning of their speech and its end; because they first stated that the legitimacy of using lottery here is an answer of istihsan and qiyas rejects it, and later they said that this is not gambling and explained the difference between it and gambling and mentioned parallels from the Book and Sunnah, which only indicates that qiyas does not reject it at all, rather qiyas also requires it, so they contradict each other.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the use of lottery (qur'ah) in the division of jointly owned property. The author states that when partners cannot agree on allocation, a lottery is conducted: the first name drawn gets the first share, the second gets the second share, and so on. This is done solely to satisfy the partners and remove dispute. An objection is raised that such a lottery is akin to gambling (qimar), which is prohibited. The response clarifies that this is not gambling because entitlement already exists; the lottery merely determines which specific share each partner receives. Gambling involves acquiring something to which one had no previous right. The practice is supported by Quranic precedents of the prophets Yunus and Zakariyya. A further objection notes an apparent contradiction: the ruling is initially presented as an exception to qiyas (analogical reasoning) via istihsan, yet later it is argued that qiyas also permits it. The text leaves this as a tension, acknowledging the debate. The Hanafi position is that lottery here is permissible and not gambling, and it is a legitimate method of division.

Key Terms
القرعة (al-qur'ah): Lottery or casting lots to allocate shares among entitled partners.
القمار (al-qimar): Gambling: acquiring something to which one had no prior right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the use of lottery (qur'ah) in division of property not considered gambling (qimar) according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the partners agree to it in advance.
B) Because entitlement to a share already exists before the lottery.
C) Because the lottery is required by the judge.
D) Because the property is not money.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits lottery in division because it merely allocates preexisting rights, unlike gambling which creates new rights.

Inclusion of Dirhams in Division Without Consent
Ruling prohibiting dirhams in division unless all consent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default Hanafi ruling on including dirhams in division of real estate, identify the exception for land with buildings, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the method of valuation.

Core Idea
Dirhams in joint property division are prohibited without consent, but necessity due to buildings on land creates an exception with differing methods among the Sahibayn.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on using money (dirhams) to equalize shares when dividing jointly owned real estate. While the default rule prohibits introducing money without unanimous consent, the presence of a building creates a practical difficulty that necessitates an exception. The text presents two approaches by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, highlighting how necessity modifies the original principle of division by measurement.

Guided Path
1
State the default ruling and its rationale
Identify the default rule: dirhams cannot be entered into the division of real estate without the consent of all partners. Understand the rationale: money is not part of the joint property, and accepting dirhams creates a debt risk for the recipient.
The default is based on the principle of avoiding gharar (uncertainty) and ensuring immediate equal ownership.
2
Identify the exceptional scenario
Recognize the exception: when the property includes a building on land, making equal division by area impossible. In this case, necessity permits the use of dirhams to achieve fairness.
The exception is triggered by practical impossibility, not mere inconvenience.
3
Analyze the two solutions of the Sahibayn
Compare Abu Yusuf's valuation method (division by value, dirhams necessarily enter) with Muhammad's offset method (land offsets building, dirhams only if residual excess remains). Note the difference in approach.
Both agree on the need for dirhams but differ on the mechanism.
4
Understand the role of necessity (darura)
Examine how the text links necessity to the abandonment of the original principle (division by measurement). The exception is approved in al-Ikhtiyar, showing it is a relied-upon position.
Necessity is measured by the inability to achieve equal division through area; it does not open the door to arbitrary use of money.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يدخل في القسمة الدراهم إلا برضائهم. يعني جماعة في أيديهم عقار، فطلبوا القسمة، وفي أحد الجانبين فضل عن الآخر، فأراد أحدهم أن يدفع عوضه من الدراهم، والآخر لم يرض بذلك، لم تدخل الدراهم في القسمة؛ لأنه لا شريك له فيها، ويفوت به التعديل في القسمة؛ لأن بعضهم يصل إلى عين المال المشترك في الحال، ودراهم الآخر في الذمة، فيخشى عليها التوى. وإذا كان أرض وبناء قسم بالقيمة عند الثاني، وتدخل الدراهم في القسمة ضرورة فإنه لا يمكن اعتبار التعديل فيه إلا بالتقويم فيرد من وقع البناء في نصيبه قيمة البناء على الآخر، وعند الثالث يرد من العرصة بمقابلة البناء، فإن بقي فضل ولا يمكن تحقيق التسوية فيه فحينئذ ترد الدراهم؛ لأن الضرورة دفع هذا القدر فلا يترك الأصل وهو القسمة بالمساحة إلا بالضرورة واستحسنه في الاختيار.
And dirhams are not entered into the division except with their consent. Meaning: a group has real estate in their hands and they request division, and in one side there is an excess over the other, so one of them wants to pay its equivalent in dirhams and the other does not agree; the dirhams are not entered into the division because he has no share in them, and equality in division would be lost because some get the actual joint property immediately while the other's dirhams are a debt, fearing loss. And if there is land and a building, division is by value according to the second (Abu Yusuf), and dirhams enter necessarily because adjustment cannot be considered except by valuation: the one in whose share the building falls pays its value to the other; and according to the third (Muhammad), the land is offset against the building; if there remains an excess and equalization cannot be achieved, then dirhams are returned because necessity permits this much, so the original principle (division by measurement) is not abandoned except by necessity, and this was approved in al-Ikhtiyar.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage discusses a ruling about including money (dirhams) in the division of jointly owned real estate. The default rule is that dirhams cannot be used to compensate for unequal shares without the consent of all partners. The reason is that money is not part of the joint property, and using it would mean one partner receives actual property while the other receives a debt, risking loss (for example, if the debtor becomes insolvent). However, there is an exception for cases involving land with a building on it. According to the second (likely Abu Yusuf), division must be by value, and dirhams must necessarily enter because adjustment cannot be made otherwise: the partner who gets the building in his share must pay the value of the building to the other. According to the third (Muhammad), the building is offset against the land; if there is remaining excess that cannot be equalized, then dirhams are used due to necessity. The text notes that this exception is based on necessity and is approved in the work al-Ikhtiyar. The Hanafi position is that the original method of division is by area, but when that is not feasible due to structures, value-based division with money may be used if necessary.

Key Terms
الدراهم (al-darahim): Money (dirhams) used to compensate for inequality in shares.
القسمة بالمساحة (al-qismah bil-masahah): Division by measurement (area) as the original method.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When can dirhams be included in division of real estate without the consent of all partners?
A) When one partner refuses to accept land.
B) When there is a building on the land and equalization is impossible by measurement.
C) When the partners agree to include money.
D) Never.

Key Takeaway
The default prohibition of dirhams in joint property division is only overridden by necessity arising from structural obstacles to equal measurement.

Division When Co-Owner Has Pathway or Water Channel
Ruling on division when a co-owner has a right of way or water channel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on division of jointly owned property when a co-owner has a pre-existing right of way or water channel, and explain why the division is annulled if the right cannot be redirected.

Core Idea
Division of joint property requires complete independence; if a co-owner's right of way cannot be removed, the division is void.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in property division (qismah) where one co-owner has a right of way or water channel across the other's share. The Hanafi school stipulates that division must achieve exclusive ownership and immediate benefit. When such encumbrances cannot be eliminated, the division fails, in contrast to a sale, where immediate benefit is not required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Recognize that the division involves property where one co-owner has a pathway (tariq) or water channel (masil) on the other's share. The ruling: if possible to redirect, it must be done; if not, the division is annulled by consensus.
The condition 'not stipulated' is key; if the right was reserved in the division, the division may stand.
2
Understand the purpose of division
The purpose of qismah is to eliminate joint ownership (qaṭʿ al-ishtirāk) and give each exclusive, beneficial use. Any residual encumbrance defeats this aim.
Contrast with sale where the aim is ownership of the corpus (milk al-raqabah), not immediate use.
3
Analyze the distinction from sale
In sale, if the buyer cannot access the property, the sale is not invalid because immediate benefit is not a condition. In division, immediate exclusive benefit is essential. This distinction (tafriq) is the legal reasoning (taʿlīl) behind the ruling.
The qiyas here is a distinction—showing why a different ruling applies.
4
Apply to a new scenario
Given two co-owners dividing land with a shared irrigation channel that passes through both shares. After division, the channel no longer services one share. The ruling: if the channel can be rerouted to the owner's share, it must be done; if impossible, the division is void.
Always check feasibility of redirection first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإلا فسخت القسمة. يعني إذا قسم العقار والحال أن لأحدهم طريقا ومسيلا في ملك الآخر، ولم يشترط في القسمة أن يكون طريقه ومسيل مائه في ملك الآخر، رفع المسيل أو الطريق عن ملك الآخر إن أمكن صرفه؛ ليتحقق معنى القسمة وهو قطع الاشتراك، وإن لم يكن صرفه فسخت القسمة إجماعا؛ لأن المقصود من القسمة تكميل المنفعة باختصاص كل بنصيبه، وقطع أسباب تعلق حق الغير، فإذا أمكن حصل المقصود، وإلا لم يحصل، فتعين الفسخ، والاستئناف على وجه يتمكن كل منهما أن يجعل لنفسه مسيلا وطريقا؛ لأن المقصود لا يتم باستطراق الغير في أرضه، وتسييله مائه في أرض غيره، وهذا بخلاف البيع حيث لا يفسخ، ولا يفسد فيما إذا لم يتمكن المشتري من الاستطراق ومن مسيل الطريق الماء؛ لأن المقصود ملك الرقبة، ولا يشترط فيه الانتفاع في الحال، ولا كذلك القسمة.
Otherwise the division is annulled. That is, if they divide real estate while one of them has a pathway and a water channel in the property of the other, and it was not stipulated in the division that his pathway and water channel remain in the other's property, the water channel or pathway is removed from the other's property if its redirection is possible, so that the meaning of division (cutting off joint ownership) is realized. If its redirection is not possible, the division is annulled by consensus, because the purpose of division is to perfect benefit by each being exclusively entitled to his share and cutting off causes of attachment of another's right. If that can be achieved, the purpose is achieved, otherwise it is not, so annulment is determined, and the division is restarted in a way that each can make for himself a water channel and pathway, because the purpose is not achieved by the other traversing his land and flowing water on another's land. This is unlike sale, where it is not annulled and is not invalid if the buyer cannot obtain a right of passage or water channel, because the purpose is ownership of the corpus, and immediate benefit is not required, unlike division.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage concerns a scenario where co-owners of a property are dividing it, but one co-owner has a pre-existing right of passage or water channel (for irrigation/drainage) that runs through the other co-owner's share. If during division this right is not explicitly preserved as a condition, the rule is: if it is possible to redirect the path or channel so that it no longer encroaches on the other's share, it should be redirected to ensure each owner's share is independent. But if redirection is impossible, the division is void (munfasikh) by consensus. The reason is that the entire purpose of division (qismah) is to eliminate shared rights and give each exclusive ownership. If one owner's right of passage remains on the other's land, the purpose is defeated. This contrasts with a sale (bay'): if a buyer purchases property and later finds that the only access is through the seller's remaining land, the sale is not void because the goal of sale is ownership of the property itself, and the right of access is not essential at the moment of sale. In division, immediate and exclusive benefit is crucial. Therefore, the division must be restructured to provide each party with independent access. This ruling is based on the principle that division is a form of exchange aimed at eliminating jointness, and any residual encumbrance defeats that aim.

Key Terms
المسيل (al-masil): Water channel or drain for irrigation or drainage.
الطريق (al-tariq): Pathway or right of way.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if after division of a property, one co-owner's right of passage remains on the other's share and cannot be redirected?
A) The division is valid but the right of passage continues.
B) The division is annulled by consensus.
C) The affected co-owner must compensate the other.
D) The judge will force a sale.

Key Takeaway
Division of joint property is void if a co-owner's right of way or water channel cannot be redirected to ensure exclusive ownership.

Division of Upper and Lower Stories: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dividing property with upper and lower floors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on dividing property with upper and lower floors and explain why Imam Muhammad's valuation method is preferred for fatwa.

Core Idea
When dividing jointly owned floors, value matters more than area—utility differences make equalization by measure impossible.

The Hanafi school is not monolithic on every detail. This passage reveals a fascinating three-way disagreement among the founding imams on how to divide a building with upper and lower floors owned jointly. While Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf agree on division by area (cubit), they differ on the ratio, and Imam Muhammad breaks away entirely, insisting on division by value. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to see how custom, utility, and legal principle interact in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
Determine the core issue: two partners jointly own a property with lower (sufl) and upper (ulu) floors, and they request division. What is the proper method?
2
State the three Hanafi positions
List the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Abu Hanifa: division by area with ratio 1:2 (lower to upper). Abu Yusuf: division by area with ratio 1:1. Muhammad: division by value after independent valuation.
These are all valid positions within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the evidence for each view
Understand the dalil behind each. Abu Hanifa: lower floor is essential (upper can be lost without lower, but not vice versa). Abu Yusuf: both serve dwelling equally. Muhammad: utilities differ (well, stable, cellar) and seasonal preferences make area equalization unfair.
These are not simply custom-based; they have principled foundations.
4
Identify the mufta bihi and tarjih
The text states that the fatwa is given on Muhammad's view. Why? Because the diversity of utilities and customs makes valuation the only equitable approach.
The tarjih authority here is the later tradition, as indicated by 'wa alayhi al-fatwa'.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa's view, the lower floor owner gets twice the area share; under Abu Yusuf, equal area; under Muhammad, each gets value proportionate to their floors' market worth.
This matters in real estate division today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سفل له علو إلخ: إذا اشترك رجلان في سفل وعلو أي بيت كامل، وفي سفل فقط، وعلوه لآخر، وفي علو فقط وسفله لآخر، وطلبا القسمة، فصورة القسمة بينهما: أن يقوم كل واحد من السفل والعلو، والسفل المجرد والعلو المجرد على حدة، ويقسم بالقيمة، ولا يعتبر بغير ذلك، وهذا هو قول الإمام محمد وعليه الفتوى وبه قالت الثلاثة، وقال الإمام والثاني يقسم بالذراع؛ لأن القسمة بالذرع الأصل في المذروع والكلام فيه والعبرة للتسوية في أصل السكنى كما في المرافق. ولمحمد الله: أن السفل يصلح لما لا يصلح له العلو كالبئر والاصطبل والسرداب وغيره فصار كالجنسين، فلا يمكنه التعديل إلا بالقيمة. ثم اختلف في كيفية القسمة على قولهما بعد أن اتفقا على القسمة بالذرع. فعند الإمام: ذراع سفل بذراعين من العلو، وقال أبو يوسف: ذراع بذراع. ثم قيل: أجاب كل واحد منهم على عادة أهل زمانه، فالإمام أجاب بناء على ما شاهد من عادة أهل الكوفة في اختيارهم السفل على العلو، وأبو يوسف سوى بناء على عادة أهل بغداد في التسوية بين العلو والسفل في منفعة السكنى، ومحمد أجاب على ما شاهد من اختلاف العادة في البلدان. وقيل هو اختلاف على الدليل، فوجه قول الإمام أن العلو يفوت بفوت السفل، ولا يفوت السفل بفوته، فتكون منفعة السفل ضعف منفعة العلو، ووجه قول أبي يوسف: أن المقصود منهما السكنى، وهما متساويان فيها، ووجه قول محمد: أن منفعة السفل والعلو متفاوتة بحسب الأوقات، ففي الصيف يختار العلو، وفي الشتاء السفل، فلا يمكن التعديل، فتقسم بالقيمة.
Lower floor, for him an upper floor etc.: If two men share in a lower and upper floor, i.e., a complete house, and in only a lower floor while its upper belongs to another, and in only an upper floor while its lower belongs to another, and they request division, the form of division between them is: each of the lower and upper floor, the mere lower and mere upper are valued separately and divided by value, and nothing else is considered. This is the statement of Imam Muhammad and upon it is the fatwa, and the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad?) said it. But Imam (Abu Hanifa) and the second (Abu Yusuf) said: divide by the cubit (area) because division by measurement is the original for measured things, and the discussion is about equality in the basic dwelling benefit, as in common facilities. For Muhammad, the lower floor is suitable for things the upper is not, like well, stable, cellar etc., so they become like two different types, and equalization is only possible by value. Then they differed on the method of division according to their two views after agreeing on division by cubit. According to Imam: one cubit of lower equals two cubits of upper; Abu Yusuf said: one cubit to one cubit. Then it was said: each answered according to the custom of his time: Imam answered based on the custom of the people of Kufa who preferred the lower floor over the upper; Abu Yusuf equalized based on the custom of Baghdad where they made no distinction; Muhammad answered based on the variation of custom in different lands. And it is said it is a difference based on evidence: the basis of Imam's view is that the upper floor is lost with the loss of the lower, but the lower is not lost with the loss of the upper, so the benefit of the lower is double that of the upper. The basis of Abu Yusuf's view is that the purpose of both is dwelling, and they are equal therein. The basis of Muhammad's view is that the benefit of lower and upper varies by season: in summer the upper is chosen, in winter the lower, so equalization is impossible, thus division by value.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the division of a property consisting of upper and lower floors (sufl and ulu) owned jointly by two partners. The discussion covers several scenarios: both jointly own a complete house, or one owns only the lower floor and the other the upper, etc. The initial question is whether to divide by area or by value. Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) holds that division must be by value because the lower and upper floors have different utilities: the lower is suitable for a well, stable, cellar, etc., making them like different types of property, so equalization by measurement is impossible. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, however, initially agree that division by area (dira') is the norm for land and buildings. But they then differ on the ratio: Abu Hanifa says one cubit of lower floor equals two cubits of upper, because the lower floor's utility is greater (the upper can be lost if the lower collapses, but not vice versa). Abu Yusuf says one cubit of lower equals one cubit of upper because both serve the same purpose of dwelling. The passage also notes that these differences may reflect the customary practices of Kufa (where lower was valued more) and Baghdad (where they were equal). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to this text is that of Imam Muhammad: division by value. The text emphasizes that in practice, the assessment must consider the specific utilities and local customs.

Key Terms
السفل (al-sufl): Lower floor or ground floor of a building.
العلو (al-ulu): Upper floor or attic.
الذرع (al-dhira'): Cubit, a unit of length; here refers to division by area measurement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in this text, how should a jointly owned property with upper and lower floors be divided?
A) By area with a ratio of 1:2 (lower to upper).
B) By area with a ratio of 1:1.
C) By value after independent valuation of each floor.
D) By auction to the highest bidder.

Key Takeaway
When dividing property where floors serve different functions, Hanafi fatwa relies on valuation rather than a fixed area ratio.
