(ملتقطا من الشروح) مثل: إن كان البذر لرب الأرض. وإن صحت الخ: يعني إذا وقعت المزارعة صحيحة، ولم يوجد فيها ما يفسدها، فالخارج من الأرض على ما شرطا لصحة الالتزام، فإن العقد إذا كان صحيحا يجب المسمى، وهذا عقد صحيح، فيجب فيه المسمى. فإن لم يخرج إلخ لأنها إما إجارة أو شركة، فإن كانت إجارة، فالواجب في العقد الصحيح منها المسمى، وهو معدوم فلا يستحق غيره وإن كانت شركة فالشركة في الخارج دون غيره، فلا يستحق غيره، بخلاف ما إذا فسدت المزارعة، ولم تخرج الأرض، حيث يستحق أجر المثل في المدة، وعدم الخروج لا يمنع وجوبه تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣١٩/٨]
It is invalid, then the produce belongs to the owner of the seed, and the other party gets the wage equivalent to his work or his land, and it does not exceed the equivalent wage of what they stipulated. If it is valid, then the produce is according to the stipulation; if nothing comes out, then nothing for the worker. It is invalid as a recompense for his saying: 'If it was' and what is coordinated with it, meaning the muzara'ah is invalid in these seven forms according to the apparent narration. And from Abu Yusuf that it is permissible in the first and second due to mutual dealing, and analogy is abandoned because of it. And because when stipulating cows with seed on the landowner became permissible, stipulating cows on him is permissible as for the worker. When stipulating cows and seed on him became permissible, stipulating cows alone on him is permissible. Al-Zayla'i said: The apparent is the first. And in al-Khaniyya: The fatwa is on the apparent narration. So the produce etc. [Basing on the invalidity of muzara'ah, i.e., if it becomes invalid, the produce etc. means if the muzara'ah becomes invalid in these seven forms, the produce from the land belongs to the owner of the seed because it is growth of his property and the branch is owned by owning the root. The other's entitlement is by name. So when it is invalid, all the growth is for the seed owner, and the other gets the wage equivalent to his work or his land. So if the seed was from the landowner, the worker gets his equivalent wage; if it was from the worker, the landowner gets the equivalent wage for his land. Then according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it does not exceed what they stipulated for him in the muzara'ah because he consented to the waiver of the excess. According to Muhammad in both cases, he gets his equivalent wage whatever it reaches because he utilized his benefits by a void contract, so its value is obligatory upon him since it has no equivalent. And the three (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar) said with Muhammad's statement. And if the muzara'ah is invalid and the seed was from the landowner, the entire produce is pure for him; if the seed was from the worker, his seed amount and what he paid as equivalent wage for the land are pure for him, and he gives charity for the surplus. (Taken from the commentaries) Example: If the seed belongs to the landowner. And 'if it is valid' etc.: meaning if the muzara'ah occurs validly and there is nothing that invalidates it, the produce from the land is according to what they stipulated because the commitment is valid. If the contract is valid, the named consideration is obligatory, and this is a valid contract, so the named consideration is obligatory. 'If nothing comes out' etc. because it is either a hire or a partnership. If it is a hire, the obligation in a valid contract is the named consideration, which is non-existent, so nothing else is entitled. If it is a partnership, the partnership is in the produce only, not in other things, so nothing else is entitled. Unlike when the muzara'ah is invalid and the land does not produce, where the equivalent wage for the period is entitled, and lack of produce does not prevent its obligation. Completion of al-Bahr al-Raiq: 8/319]
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the consequences of a muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract that is either invalid (fasid) or valid (sahih). The author begins by stating that if the contract is invalid, the produce belongs to the owner of the seed, while the other party (the worker or landowner) receives an equivalent wage (ajr al-mithl) for their contribution, not exceeding the wage they had stipulated. This is because a fasid contract does not transfer ownership; the produce is a growth of the seed owner's property. The text then notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to the Zahir al-Riwayah, certain forms of muzara'ah are invalid, but Abu Yusuf permits the first two forms based on customary practice ('urf) and istihsan, arguing that stipulating cows with seed on the landowner is analogous to stipulating cows on the worker. Al-Zayla'i prefers the Zahir al-Riwayah, and the fatwa is on that. The commentary elaborates: in a fasid contract, the seed owner gets the produce, and the other gets ajr al-mithl. If the seed is from the landowner, the worker gets ajr al-mithl; if from the worker, the landowner gets ajr al-mithl for his land. There is a difference between Abu Yusuf/Muhammad and Muhammad al-Shaybani: the former limit the ajr to the stipulated amount, while Muhammad says it is unlimited because the benefits were consumed under a void contract. The three (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar) agree with Muhammad. Purity (tayyib) of earnings is also discussed: the seed owner's share is pure; the worker's share is pure only to the extent of his seed and expenses; the surplus must be given in charity. For a valid contract, the produce is distributed as stipulated, and if no produce is harvested, the worker gets nothing because the contract is based on production. This is contrasted with a fasid contract where ajr al-mithl is still due even with no produce.

Key Terms
المزارعة (al-muzāraʿah): A sharecropping contract where one party provides land and seed and the other provides labor, with produce shared by agreement.
فسدت (fasidat): The contract is invalid due to a defect in its essential elements or conditions.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The fair market wage for the work performed or the rental value of the land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is divided equally between the landowner and the worker.
B) It belongs entirely to the owner of the seed.
C) It is given in charity.
D) It belongs to the worker who performed the labor.

Key Takeaway
In a fasid muzara'ah, produce goes to the seed owner and the other party gets ajr al-mithl (capped by stipulation); in a valid one, produce is shared per stipulation and no crop means no pay.

Compulsion to Perform the Muzara'ah Contract
Discusses compulsion to perform muzara'ah contract.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the owner of the seed is not compelled to proceed with a muzara'ah contract and state the ethical obligation to pay ajr al-mithl.

Core Idea
In a binding muzara'ah, the seed owner is not compelled to proceed because it would destroy his property without guarantee of return.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on legal compulsion (ijbar) in the muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract. The matn states that both parties are compelled to fulfill their obligations, except the owner of the seed (rabb al-badhr). The commentary draws an analogy to a hire contract for demolition, illustrating the reasoning. We will explore the basis of this exception and its practical consequences, including the ethical duty to pay the worker an equivalent wage when the seed owner backs out after work has been done.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule of compulsion
The matn says: 'Whoever refuses to proceed is compelled, except the owner of the seed.' This means both parties (worker and seed owner) are generally compelled, but seed owner is an exception.
General rule: both compelled; exception: seed owner.
2
Identify the reason for the exception
The seed owner cannot proceed without destroying his property (scattering seed) with uncertain outcome. Thus he is not compelled. This is likened to hiring to demolish a house: the hiree is compelled but the owner is not.
Analogy to demolition hire.
3
Understand the consequence if seed owner refuses after work done
If the seed owner refuses after the worker has tilled, the worker gets no compensation in court (qada'an) because his work was valued by the contract share, which doesn't exist. But ethically (bainahu wa bain Allah), he must receive ajr al-mithl.
Court vs ethical obligation.
4
Note the fatwa
The fatwa is to satisfy the worker by paying ajr al-mithl, as stated in Ramz al-Haqaiq.
Mufta bihi position.

Source Text

ومن أبى عن المضي، أجبر إلا رب البذر . امتنع من العاقدين على ما التزم من العمل فإنه لا يجبر عند الإباء فسدت جزاء لقوله: "فإن كانت" وما عطف عليه أي فسدت المزارعة في هذه الوجوه السبعة في ظاهر الرواية، وقد بين وجه فساد كل صورة عند بيانها، وعن أبي يوسف أنه يجوز في الأولى والثانية؛ للتعامل، والقياس يترك به، ولأنه لما جاز شرط البقر مع البذر على رب الأرض، جاز شرط البقر عليه كما في العامل، لما جاز شرط البقر والبذر عليه جاز شرط البقر وحده عليه قال الزيلعي والظاهر هو الأول، وفي "الخانية": والفتوى على ظاهر الرواية. فيكون الخارج إلخ [تفريع على فساد المزارعة أي إذا فسدت يكون الخارج إلخ يعني إذا فسدت المزارعة في هذه الوجوه السبعة، يكون الخارج من الأرض لرب البذر؛ لأنه نماء ملكه والفرع يملك بملك الأصل، واستحقاق الآخر بالتسمية، فإذا فسدت كان النماء كله لرب البذر، وللآخر أجر مثل عمله أو أرضه، فلو كان البذر من رب الأرض، فللعامل أجر مثله، وإن كان من قبل العامل، فلرب الأرض أجر مثل أرضه، ثم عندهما لا يزاد على ما شرطا له بالمزارعة؛ لأنه رضي بسقوط الزيادة، وعند محمد في الفصلين له أجر مثله بالغا ما بلغ؛ لأنه استوفى منافعه بعقد فاسد، فيجب عليه قيمتها؛ إذ لا مثل لها، وبقول محمد قالت الثلاثة. وإذا فسدت المزارعة، والبذر من قبل رب الأرض، طاب له الخارج كله وإن كان البذر من قبل العامل طاب له قدر بذره، وقدر ما غرم من أجر مثل الأرض، وتصدق بالفضل. (ملتقطا من الشروح) مثل: إن كان البذر لرب الأرض. وإن صحت الخ: يعني إذا وقعت المزارعة صحيحة، ولم يوجد فيها ما يفسدها، فالخارج من الأرض على ما شرطا لصحة الالتزام، فإن العقد إذا كان صحيحا يجب المسمى، وهذا عقد صحيح، فيجب فيه المسمى. فإن لم يخرج إلخ لأنها إما إجارة أو شركة، فإن كانت إجارة، فالواجب في العقد الصحيح منها المسمى، وهو معدوم فلا يستحق غيره وإن كانت شركة فالشركة في الخارج دون غيره، فلا يستحق غيره، بخلاف ما إذا فسدت المزارعة، ولم تخرج الأرض، حيث يستحق أجر المثل في المدة، وعدم الخروج لا يمنع وجوبه تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣١٩/٨] ومن أبى عن المضي إلخ: يعني ومن امتنع من المتعاقدين عن المضي على ما التزم أجبر على العمل؛ لأنها انعقدت إجارة، وهي عقد لازم، إلا رب البذر ، فإنه لا يجبر عند الإباء؛ لأنه لا يمكنه المضي إلا بإتلاف ماله، وهو لقاء البذر على الأرض، ولا يدري هل يخرج أم لا، فصار نظير ما لو استأجر ليهدم داره، ثم امتنع، فإن امتنع العامل، أجبر على العمل؛ لأنه لا يلحقه به ضرر ثم إذا امتنع رب البذر - والأرض من قبله - بعد ما كرب المزارع الأرض، فلا شيء له في عمل الكراب في القضاء؛ لأن عمله إنما يتقوم بالعقد، وقد قومه بجزء من الخارج، ولا خارج، الله : ويلزمه فيما بينه وبين تعالى أن يعطيه أجر مثل عمله كي لا يكون مغرورا من جهته؛ لأنه يتضرر به، وهو مدفوع، فيفتى بإرضائه بأن يوفيه أجر مثله رمز الحقائق: ٣٥٦/٢]
And whoever refuses to proceed is compelled, except the owner of the seed. The contractors refrain from what they committed of work, but he is not compelled at refusal. It is invalid as a recompense for his saying: 'If it was' and what is coordinated with it... [repetition] ... And from Abu Yusuf... [repetition] ... And from 'whoever refuses to proceed' etc.: meaning whoever from the two contractors refrains from proceeding on what he committed is compelled to work because it is a hire contract that is binding, except the owner of the seed, for he is not compelled at refusal because he cannot proceed except by destroying his property, namely scattering the seed on the land, and he does not know whether it will come out or not. So it is like the case of one who hires to demolish his house and then refuses. If the worker refuses, he is compelled to work because no harm befalls him. Then if the seed owner refuses—and the land is from him—after the sharecropper has tilled the land, he (the worker) gets nothing for the work of tilling according to judicial ruling because his work is valued by the contract, and he has valued it by a portion of the produce, and there is no produce. But between him and Allah Almighty, he must give him the equivalent wage for his work so that he is not deceived by his act, because he is harmed by him, and he (the worker) is repelled. So it is issued a fatwa to satisfy him by paying him his equivalent wage. (Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/356]
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This section addresses the compulsion (jabr) of parties to fulfill a muzara'ah contract. The matn states that if either party refuses to proceed, they are compelled (i.e., taken to court and forced to perform), except for the owner of the seed (rabb al-badhr), who cannot be compelled. The commentary explains the reason: the contract is essentially a hire (ijarah), which is a binding contract. Therefore, the worker is compelled to perform the labor because it does not cause him loss. But the seed owner cannot be forced because he would have to scatter his seed on the land, which is a destruction of his property, and he does not know if the crop will grow. This is likened to a case where someone hires a worker to demolish his house and then refuses—the worker is compelled, but the owner is not because it involves destruction of his property. However, if the seed owner refuses after the worker has already performed land preparation (such as tilling), the worker is not entitled to compensation in court (qada'an) because his work was valued by the contract in exchange for a share of the produce, which does not exist. But ethically (bainahu wa bain Allah), the seed owner is obligated to pay the worker an equivalent wage (ajr al-mithl) so that the worker is not deceived. The fatwa is to satisfy him by paying the ajr al-mithl, as stated in Ramz al-Haqaiq.

Key Terms
الإجبار (al-ijbār): Legal compulsion to fulfill a contractual obligation.
رب البذر (rabb al-badhr): The owner of the seed, one of the parties in muzara'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the owner of the seed (rabb al-badhr) not compelled to proceed with the muzara'ah?
A) Because he is outside the contract.
B) Because he would have to destroy his property (scatter seed) without knowing if the crop will grow.
C) Because the worker is the one who must sow the seed.
D) Because the contract is not binding on him.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi muzara'ah, the seed owner cannot be compelled to proceed because of the risk to his property, but he must ethically compensate the worker for labor already performed.

Termination of Muzara'ah by Death of a Party
Explains termination of muzara'ah upon death with istihsan exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the termination of a muzara'ah contract upon the death of a party, apply the istihsan exception when the crop has grown, and determine the worker's compensation in related scenarios.

Core Idea
A muzara'ah contract dissolves with death, but istihsan preserves it if the crop has grown to protect sharecroppers' rights.

This lesson examines the effect of death on a muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract. While the default analogy with hire leads to immediate invalidity (qiyas), Hanafi jurists apply istihsan to allow the contract to continue until harvest if the crop has already sprouted. We will also explore related cases involving land preparation and debt that affect the contract and compensation.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the qiyas ruling
Understand that muzara'ah is analogous to a hire contract; like hire, it becomes invalid (batil) upon the death of either party because the contract is personal.
The text explicitly says 'لأنها إجارة' (because it is a hire).
2
Identify the istihsan exception
If the crop has already grown at the time of death, the contract continues until harvest to allow the crop to be gathered and divided. This is based on maslaha (consideration of rights).
The exception applies only if the crop has sprouted ('نبت الزرع').
3
Apply the rule to landowner's death after land preparation
If the landowner dies after tilling and digging canals but before planting, the contract is rescinded and the worker gets nothing because his work was only compensated by a share of nonexistent produce.
This contrasts with the earlier case where the worker is deceived by the seed owner – here there is no produce to justify payment.
4
Analyze the debt scenario
If the landowner has a debt and must sell the land before planting, the contract is dissolved and the worker gets nothing for preparatory work. But if the crop has grown, the land cannot be sold until the crop is harvested to protect the sharecropper's right.
The judge may even release the landowner from imprisonment to allow time for harvesting.
5
Synthesize the principles
The key is the presence or absence of a growing crop. When no crop exists, the strict qiyas applies and the worker gets no compensation. When a crop exists, istihsan overrides to preserve the crop and the contract until harvest.
This illustrates the Hanafi method of balancing analogy with public interest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتبطل بموت أحدهما، وتبطل إلخ لأنها إجارة، وهي تبطل بموت أحد المتعاقدين إذا عقدها لنفسه، وقد بيناه في الإجارة، وهذا الإطلاق في البطلان جواب القياس وفي الاستحسان: إذا مات وقد نبت الزرع، يبقى عقد الإجارة حتى يحصد الزرع، ثم يبطل في الباقي من المدة؛ لأن في إبقائه هذه المدة مراعاة الحقين فيعمل العامل، أو وارثه على حاله، فإذا حصد يقسم على ما شرطاه، ولا ضرورة في الباقي، ولو مات رب الأرض قبل الزرع بعد ما كرب الأرض، وحفر الأنهار، انتقضت المزارعة؛ لأنه ليس في ذلك إتلاف مال على الزارع ولا شيء للعامل بمقابلة العمل؛ لأنه يقوم بالخارج، ولا خارج، فلا يجب شيء. بخلاف المسألة الأولى حيث يقضى بإرضائه؛ لأنه مغرور من جهته باختياره، وإذا كان على رب الأرض دين، ولم يقدر على قضائه إلا ببيع الأرض، فسخت المزارعة قبل الزرع وبيعت بالدين، ولا شيء للعامل عليه في الكرب وحفر الأنهار، ولو نبت الزرع ولم يحصد لم تبع الأرض بالدين حتى يستحصد الزرع؛ لأن في البيع إبطال حق المزارع، والتأخير أهون من الإبطال، ويخرجه القاضي من الحبس إن كان الحبس من أ أجله . [ تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٢٠/٨]
And it becomes invalid with the death of one of them. 'And it becomes invalid' etc. because it is a hire, and it becomes invalid upon the death of one of the two contractors if he contracted it for himself, and we have explained that in the chapter of hire. This absolute statement of invalidity is the answer of analogy. In istihsan: if he dies and the crop has grown, the hire contract remains until the crop is harvested, then it becomes invalid for the remainder of the term, because in keeping it for this term there is consideration of the rights of both. So the worker or his heir continues in his state, and when harvested, it is divided according to their stipulation, and there is no need for the remainder. If the landowner dies before planting after having tilled the land and dug canals, the muzara'ah is rescinded because there is no destruction of the worker's property, and the worker is entitled to nothing in exchange for the work because it is valued by the produce, and there is no produce, so nothing is due. Unlike the previous case where he is decreed satisfaction because he was deceived by his own choice. And if the landowner has a debt and cannot pay it except by selling the land, the muzara'ah is dissolved before planting and the land is sold for the debt, and the worker has nothing against him for the tilling and digging canals. If the crop has grown but not been harvested, the land is not sold for the debt until the crop is harvested, because selling would nullify the sharecropper's right, and delay is easier than nullification. And the judge releases him from imprisonment if the imprisonment was for his debt. [Completion of al-Bahr al-Raiq: 8/320]
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This lesson covers the dissolution of a muzara'ah contract upon the death of either party. The general rule (qiyas) is that the contract becomes invalid (batil) immediately because it is a hire agreement that terminates with death. However, there is an istihsan (juristic preference) that if the crop has already sprouted, the contract remains valid until harvest so that the crop can be saved and divided as stipulated. The worker or his heir continues the work. If the landowner dies before planting but after land preparation (tilling, digging canals), the contract is rescinded and the worker gets nothing because his work was only compensated by a share of the crop, which does not exist. This is contrasted with the earlier case of the seed owner's refusal where the worker gets ajr al-mithl ethically. Then an additional scenario: if the landowner has a debt and must sell the land, if the crop has not been planted, the muzara'ah is dissolved and the land sold; the worker gets nothing for preparatory work. If the crop has already grown, the land cannot be sold until the crop is harvested to protect the sharecropper's right. The judge even releases the landowner from imprisonment to allow time for harvesting.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas for a stronger reason, such as necessity or custom.
موت أحد المتعاقدين (mawt aḥad al-mutaʿāqidayn): Death of either party to the contract, which normally terminates a hire contract.
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical reasoning used to extend a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared effective cause.
الزرع (al-zarʿ): The crop that is grown; its presence before death triggers the istihsan exception.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under istihsan, when does a muzara'ah contract continue after the death of one party?
A) When the worker dies.
B) When the landowner dies before any work.
C) When the crop has already grown.
D) In all cases.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses istihsan to protect the crop and the worker's right, overriding the strict analogy with hire when the crop has already grown.

Post-Term Obligations in Muzara'ah
Determines obligations of worker and landowner when the contract term ends before the crop is ready.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two obligations that arise when a muzara'ah term expires before the crop is harvested, and explain the reasoning (ta'lil) behind each.

Core Idea
When a muzara'ah ends before harvest, the worker pays rent for the land and both share crop expenses proportionally.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario in sharecropping: what happens if the agreed term ends but the crop is not yet ready? The matn lays down two clear obligations: the worker must pay rent for the continued use of the land, and both parties share the crop's expenses according to their ownership shares. We will unpack the legal reasoning behind each rule, including the distinction from the death of the worker.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the muzara'ah contract has a fixed term that expires while the crop is still unripe. The crop cannot be uprooted without harm.
The scenario presupposes a valid muzara'ah contract that has ended by term expiry.
2
State the first obligation
The worker (muzari') must pay ajr al-mithl (equivalent rent) for the land from the term expiry until the crop is harvested.
The rent is not the full plot rent but only for the share of land the crop occupies.
3
Explain the reasoning for rent
The contract is ended, but uprooting causes harm. The crop is allowed to remain by paying rent. The worker benefits from the land, so he must compensate the owner.
This is ta'lil based on harm avoidance (darar) and istihsan.
4
State the second obligation
Both the landowner and the worker share the expenses of the crop (nafaqat al-zar') after term expiry in proportion to their ownership shares.
Expenses include watering, fertilizing, harvesting costs, etc.
5
Explain the reasoning for expenses
After term expiry, the crop is jointly owned. Expenses incurred to preserve and harvest it are shared. Before expiry, the worker bears all labor costs as part of his contractual duty.
The original contract obliges the worker to cultivate until the crop is complete, but after term, it becomes a joint venture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If the term passes and the crop has not yet ripened, then on the sharecropper is the equivalent rent of the muzara'ah, i.e., one of the two contractors, i.e., the term of the muzara'ah while the crop has not reached harvest until it ripens. And the expenses of the crop are on both of them according to their shares. 'On the sharecropper' etc.: meaning it is obligatory on the worker to pay the equivalent rent of the other's land until the crop is harvested. The apparent wording is that he must pay the entire rent, but it is not so. If he said 'what is in his share' it would be better and safer. The reason for the obligation of rent is that the contract has ended with the passing of the term, and uprooting would cause harm, so we kept it with an equivalent rent until it is harvested. So the rent is obligatory on the one who is not the owner of the land according to his share, because he utilized the benefit of the land to that extent. Unlike the case where one dies before the crop ripens, where it is left to harvest and nothing is owed on the sharecropper because we kept the hire contract here by istihsan, so it is possible for the worker to continue his work. But here, retention is not possible because the term has expired. Commentary
This lesson deals with the scenario where the fixed term of a muzara'ah contract ends before the crop is ready for harvest. The matn states two obligations: (1) The sharecropper (muzari', i.e., the worker) must pay ajr al-mithl (equivalent rent) for the use of the land until the crop can be harvested. (2) Both parties share the expenses of the crop (nafaqat al-zar') in proportion to their ownership shares. The commentary clarifies that the rent is not the full plot rent, but only the share corresponding to the portion the crop occupies. The reason is that the contract has ended, but uprooting the crop would cause harm, so the crop is allowed to remain with the payment of rent. This is contrasted with the case of death where the contract is preserved by istihsan. Regarding expenses, the worker is responsible for all labor expenses before the crop ripens (such as watering, weeding) as part of his obligation under the original contract. After the term expires, expenses for harvesting and marketing are shared according to ownership shares. The text ends mid-sentence.

Key Terms
المزارع (al-muzāriʿ): The sharecropper, i.e., the worker who cultivates the land.
نفقة الزرع (nafaqat al-zarʿ): Expenses of the crop, including labor, water, fertilizer, and harvesting costs.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The equivalent rent, i.e., the market rate for similar land use.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only the landowner pays all expenses.
C) Both parties share expenses proportionally.
D) No one pays; expenses are waived.

Key Takeaway
After a muzara'ah term expires before harvest, the worker owes rent for continued land use, and both parties share crop expenses in proportion to ownership.

Termination of Muzara'ah: Death and Expiry of Term
Ruling with proof on muzara'ah termination

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a muzara'ah contract ends due to death or term expiry before crop ripens, and explain the application of istihsan vs qiyas.

Core Idea
When muzara'ah ends prematurely, the worker pays ujr al-mithl and expenses are shared—an istihsan exception to protect both parties.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on what happens when a sharecropping (muzara'ah) contract is cut short—either by the death of one party or by the expiry of the agreed term before the crop is ready to harvest. The rulings balance the general rule that such contracts are void upon death (qiyas) with the need to avoid wasting the worker's labor and the growing crop (istihsan). You will learn when the contract remains in effect, what the worker must pay, and how expenses are divided.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two termination scenarios
The passage covers two distinct scenarios: (1) death of one party, and (2) expiry of the fixed term while the crop is still unripe. Note that each has a different default ruling based on qiyas and istihsan.
Death of the landowner before planting is treated separately from death after crop sprouts.
2
Apply the rule of qiyas for death
According to strict analogy (qiyas), muzara'ah as a form of ijara is invalidated by death. State this as the baseline ruling.
The text says 'this absolute statement of invalidity is the answer of qiyas'.
3
Apply istihsan when crop exists
If the crop has already sprouted at the time of death, istihsan keeps the contract valid until harvest to protect both parties' rights. The worker or his heir continues, and the produce is divided as agreed.
This overrides the qiyas ruling for the sake of equity.
4
Determine the worker's obligation on term expiry
If the term expires before the crop ripens, the contract ends, but the worker must pay ujr al-mithl (equivalent wage) for the landowner's share of the land benefit. Both parties share crop expenses proportionally.
Ujr al-mithl is due because the worker continues to benefit from the land without a valid contract.
5
Handle special cases: landowner debt
If the landowner owes debts, the land may be sold, but if the crop is growing, sale is delayed until harvest to preserve the worker's rights.
This shows priority of the worker's interest in the growing crop over creditors.

وتبطل إلخ لأنها إجارة، وهي تبطل بموت أحد المتعاقدين إذا عقدها لنفسه، وقد بيناه في الإجارة، وهذا الإطلاق في البطلان جواب القياس وفي الاستحسان: إذا مات وقد نبت الزرع، يبقى عقد الإجارة حتى يحصد الزرع، ثم يبطل في الباقي من المدة؛ لأن في إبقائه هذه المدة مراعاة الحقين فيعمل العامل، أو وارثه على حاله، فإذا حصد يقسم على ما شرطاه، ولا ضرورة في الباقي، ولو مات رب الأرض قبل الزرع بعد ما كرب الأرض، وحفر الأنهار، انتقضت المزارعة؛ لأنه ليس في ذلك إتلاف مال على الزارع ولا شيء للعامل بمقابلة العمل؛ لأنه يقوم بالخارج، ولا خارج، فلا يجب شيء.
بخلاف المسألة الأولى حيث يقضى بإرضائه؛ لأنه مغرور من جهته باختياره، وإذا كان على رب الأرض دين، ولم يقدر على قضائه إلا ببيع الأرض، فسخت المزارعة قبل الزرع وبيعت بالدين، ولا شيء للعامل عليه في الكرب وحفر الأنهار، ولو نبت الزرع ولم يحصد لم تبع الأرض بالدين حتى يستحصد الزرع؛ لأن في البيع إبطال حق المزارع، والتأخير أهون من الإبطال، ويخرجه القاضي من الحبس إن كان الحبس من أ أجله . [ تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٢٠/٨] فعلى المزارع إلخ: يعني يجب على العامل أجر مثل أرض الآخر حتى يستحصد، وظاهر العبارة أنه يجب عليه جميع الأجرة، وليس كذلك، فلو قال: "ما في نصيبه لكان أولى وأسلم ووجه وجوب الأجر: أن العقد قد انتهى بمضي المدة، وفي القلع ضرر، فأبقيناه بأجر المثل إلى أن يستحصد، فيجب على غير صاحب الأرض بحصته . الأجرة؛ لأنه من استوفى منفعة الأرض بقدره، بخلاف ما لو مات قبل إدراك الزرع حيث يترك إلى الحصاد، ولا يجب على المزارع شيء؛ لأنا أبقينا عقد الإجارة هنا استحسانا، فأمكن استمرار العامل على ما كان من العمل، أما هنا فلا يمكن الإبقاء لانقضاء المدة تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٢١/٨]
11
ونفقة الزرع إلخ : يعني إذا انقضت مدة المزارعة قبل إدراك الزرع، تجب عليهما نفقة الزرع على قدر ملكهما، كما يجب عليهما أجرة الحصاد وأمثاله مطلقا من غير قيد بانقضاء مدة المزارعة، أما نفقة الزرع بعد انقضاء المدة؛ فلما بينا، وأما وجوب الحصاد وما ذكر فلأن عقد المزارعة يوجب على العامل عملا يحتاج إليه إلى انتهاء الزرع؛ ليزداد الزرع بذلك، فيبقى ذلك باشتراك بينهما، فيجب عليهما. والحاصل أن ما كان مؤنة العمل قبل بلوغ الزرع مما يصلح به الزرع، فهو على العامل؛ لأن ذلك على المزارعة،
Book of Muzara'ah. Rulings of Muzara'ah: It (the contract) is invalidated by the death of one of them. If the term passes and the crop has not ripened, then upon the muzari' (worker) is the ujr al-mithl (equivalent wage) of the muzara'ah—meaning one of the two contracting parties, meaning the term of the muzara'ah, while the crop has not reached harvest [?] until it ripens—and the expenses of the crop are upon both of them according to their rights. His land. And he harvests after the expiry of the term of the muzara'ah, meaning according to their ownership. So he has nothing for the work of digging in the court; because his work is only valued by the contract, and it valued it by a part of the produce, and there is no produce. Allah: and it is binding upon him between him and the Exalted to give him the equivalent of his work so that he is not deceived from his side; because he is harmed by it, and he is compelled, so it is given as a fatwa to satisfy him by paying him its equivalent [Ramz al-Haqaiq 2:356]. 'And it is invalidated' etc. because it is an ijara, and it is invalidated by the death of one of the contracting parties if he contracted it for himself, and we have explained it in the book of Ijara. This absolute statement of invalidity is the answer of qiyas, and in istihsan: if he dies and the crop has sprouted, the contract of ijara remains until the crop is harvested, then it becomes invalid in the remaining period; because in keeping it for this period is consideration of both rights, so the worker or his heir works as before, and when harvested it is divided according to their stipulation, and there is no necessity in the remainder. And if the landowner dies before planting, after he has tilled the land and dug the canals, the muzara'ah is annulled; because there is no destruction of the worker's property, and the worker has nothing in return for the work; because it is valued by the produce, and there is no produce, so nothing is obligatory. Unlike the first case where he is ordered to be satisfied; because he is deceived from his side by his choice. And if the landowner has a debt and cannot repay it except by selling the land, the muzara'ah is dissolved before planting and the land is sold for the debt, and the worker has nothing for the tilling and digging canals. But if the crop has sprouted and not yet harvested, the land is not sold for debt until the crop is harvested; because in selling there is annulment of the worker's right, and delay is easier than annulment, and the judge removes him from prison if the imprisonment was for it. [Takmilat al-Bahr al-Raiq 8:320]. 'So upon the muzari'' etc.: meaning that the worker must pay the ujr al-mithl of the other's land until the crop is harvested, and the apparent meaning of the phrase is that he must pay all the wage, but it is not so; if he said 'what is in his share would be more appropriate and safer'. And the reason for the obligation of the wage: that the contract has ended with the passage of the term, and in uprooting there is harm, so we keep it with ujr al-mithl until it is harvested, so it is obligatory upon the one who is not the owner of the land according to his share of the wage; because he has received the benefit of the land to his extent, unlike the case where he dies before the ripening of the crop where it is left until harvest, and nothing is obligatory upon the muzari'; because we have kept the ijara contract here via istihsan, so the worker can continue his work, but here it cannot be kept because the term has expired [Takmilat al-Bahr al-Raiq 8:321]. 'And the expenses of the crop' etc.: meaning that if the term of the muzara'ah expires before the crop ripens, the expenses of the crop are obligatory upon both of them according to their ownership, just as the wages of harvesting and the like are obligatory upon them absolutely without restriction of expiry of term. As for the expenses of the crop after the expiry of the term, it is as we have stated; as for the obligation of harvesting and what was mentioned, it is because the contract of muzara'ah obligates upon the worker work needed until the end of the crop, so that the crop increases thereby, so it remains shared between them, so it is obligatory upon both. And the summary: that what is a cost of work before the ripening of the crop that improves the crop is upon the worker; because that is upon the muzara'ah.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Kanz al-Daqaiq and its commentary. It addresses the situation when a muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract ends prematurely due to the death of one party or the expiry of the term before the crop is ripe. The ruling states that the contract is invalidated by death, but if the term ends and the crop is not ripe, the worker (muzari') must pay an ujr al-mithl (equivalent wage) for the landowner's share, and both parties bear the crop expenses proportionally. The commentary explains that this is based on the nature of the contract as an ijara (lease) and provides a distinction between qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference). According to qiyas, the contract is void ab initio, but by istihsan, if the crop has already sprouted, the contract remains effective until harvest to protect both parties' interests. If the landowner dies before planting, the worker gets nothing for his work. If the landowner has debts, the land may be sold, but if the crop is growing, sale is delayed until harvest. The worker must pay ujr al-mithl because he continues to benefit from the land after the contract ends, and the expense of harvesting and similar tasks are shared because the contract obligates work up to the end of the crop season. The summary clarifies that pre-ripening work costs are on the worker, while post-ripening costs and those after the term are shared proportionally.

Key Terms
مزارعة (muzara'ah): A sharecropping contract where the landowner provides land and the worker provides labor, and the produce is shared according to agreed proportions.
أجر المثل (ujr al-mithl): The equivalent wage for the use of the land, determined by market rates or fair estimation, paid by the worker to the landowner when the contract ends.
الاستحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference where the ruling deviates from strict analogy (qiyas) for reasons of equity and necessity, as in keeping the contract valid after death to avoid loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a muzara'ah contract, the landowner has a debt and needs to sell the land. If the crop has sprouted but is not yet harvested, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The land is sold immediately, and the worker loses his share.
B) The sale is delayed until the crop is harvested to protect the worker's rights.
C) The worker must buy the land to save the crop.
D) The contract is void, and the worker gets nothing.

Key Takeaway
When a muzara'ah contract ends prematurely, the worker may owe ujr al-mithl and both parties share expenses, with istihsan overriding qiyas to protect existing crops.

Stipulating Post-Harvest Works in Muzara'ah: Custom Overriding Qiyas
Ruling on conditioning certain post-harvest works on the worker in muzara'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi dispute on stipulating post-harvest works in muzara'ah and explain why the later fatwa follows Abu Yusuf based on custom.

Core Idea
Custom can override qiyas: stipulating post-harvest works on the worker is valid by custom, even though qiyas would invalidate the contract.

In a muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract, the worker is usually responsible for agricultural work. But what if the parties stipulate that the worker must also do post-harvest tasks like carrying, threshing, and winnowing? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute: while the base ruling deems such conditions invalid, later fatwa permits them due to prevailing custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the stipulated works
The passage defines four post-harvest works: al-hisad (harvesting), al-rafa' (carrying to the threshing floor), al-diyasah (threshing), and al-tadhriyah (winnowing). Note that these are distinct from the agricultural work of tending the crop.
These terms are explained with references to Ramz al-Haqaiq.
2
State the base ruling and its qiyas-based reasoning
According to the matn (Kanz al-Daqaiq), stipulating any of these works on the worker corrupts the contract (fasid). The reason: these works are not required by the contract (which only demands agricultural work), so they are extraneous conditions that invalidate the contract, analogous to stipulating carrying or grinding on the worker.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, consistent with Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Identify Abu Yusuf's alternative position
The passage reports a narration from Abu Yusuf that such stipulations are permissible (ja'iz). This view is not based on qiyas but on the prevailing custom (تعامل) among the people of Balkh.
Abu Yusuf's view is a Nawadir report, but it becomes the mufta bihi.
4
Understand the fatwa based on custom
The author of al-Multaqa states that the fatwa is according to Abu Yusuf, and the scholars of Balkh gave fatwa permitting even stipulating expenses and carrying to the worker's house due to custom. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani chose this as the most correct (al-asahh). The principle: custom can override qiyas.
This shows how later Hanafi jurists adapted rulings to societal needs.
5
Recognize the limit: works not supported by custom
The passage ends with a consensus point: if they stipulate al-jidad (picking dates) on the worker, and harvesting on the other party, it is not permissible by consensus because there is no custom (تعامل) to support it. This shows that the custom-based exception is not unlimited.
Jidad is a specific task for dates, not grains; custom does not cover it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

والرفاع: هو حمل الزرع بعد الحصاد إلى البيدر. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٥٧/٢]
والدياسة: من الدوس وهو دوس الزرع بالبقر ليخرج الحب. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٥٧/٢]
والتذرية من ذرى يذري في الهواء ليخرج الحب، ويتميز التبن. رمز الحقائق: ٣٥٧/٢] فإن شرطاه إلخ : يعني إن شرطا العمل الذي يكون بعد انتهاء الزرع كالحصاد من وما ذكرناه على العامل، فسدت المزارعة؛ لأنه شرط لا يقتضيه العقد، وإنما قلنا ذلك؛ لأن العقد يقتضي عمل المزارع، وهذه الأشياء ليست من أفعال الزرع، فكانت أجنبية، فيكون شرطها مفسدا كشرط الحمل والطحن على العامل تكملة البحر الرائق: ۳۲۲/۸] وروي عن أبي يوسف: أنه يجوز.
قال في "الملتقى: وعليه الفتوى ومشايخ بلخ أفتوا به وقالوا يجوز شرط النفقة والحمل إلى منزله على العامل أيضا؛ للتعامل بين الناس، والقياس يترك به، واختاره شمس الأئمة، وقال إنه الأصح، ولو شرطا الجداد على العامل والحصاد على غير العامل لا يجوز بالإجماع؛ لعدم التعامل. (تكملة، فتح)
And it (harvesting) is cutting the crop. And al-rafa': it is carrying the crop after harvest to the threshing floor. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 2:357]. And al-diyasah: from dawasa, and it is treading the crop with cattle to extract the grain. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 2:357]. And al-tadhriyah: from dharra, he winnows in the air to extract the grain, and the straw becomes separated. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 2:357]. 'Then if they stipulate' etc.: meaning if they stipulate the work that is after the completion of the crop such as harvesting from what we have mentioned upon the worker, the muzara'ah is corrupted; because it is a condition not required by the contract. And we only say that because the contract requires the work of the muzari', and these things are not from the actions of agriculture, so they are extraneous, thus their stipulation is corrupting like stipulating carrying and grinding upon the worker [Takmilat al-Bahr al-Raiq 8:322]. And it is reported from Abu Yusuf that it is permissible. He said in al-Multaqa: 'And upon it is the fatwa, and the scholars of Balkh gave fatwa with it and said it is permissible to stipulate the expense and carrying to his house upon the worker also, due to the custom of the people, and qiyas is abandoned by it, and Shams al-A'imma chose it and said it is the most correct.' And if they stipulate al-jidad (picking dates) upon the worker and harvesting upon the other, it is not permissible by consensus, due to lack of custom. (Takmila, Fath)
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage defines key agricultural terms and then addresses the validity of stipulating certain post-harvest works on the worker in a muzara'ah contract. The works include: الحصاد (harvesting), الرفاع (carrying to the threshing floor), الدياسة (threshing), and التذرية (winnowing). The base ruling from the matn (Kanz al-Daqaiq) is that stipulating any of these works on the worker corrupts the contract. The reason given is that these works are not part of the agricultural work required by the contract (which is tending the crop from planting to ripening); they are extraneous, and their stipulation invalidates the contract just as stipulating unrelated tasks like carrying or grinding would. However, the commentary reports a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf that such stipulations are permissible. Furthermore, the author of al-Multaqa states that the fatwa is according to Abu Yusuf, and the scholars of Balkh also gave fatwa allowing stipulating expenses and carrying to the worker's house due to prevailing custom (تعامل) which overrides qiyas. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani chose this as the most correct position. The passage ends by noting that if they stipulate الجداد (picking dates, a different task) on the worker and harvesting on the other party, it is not permissible by consensus because there is no custom supporting it. Thus, the lesson illustrates an intra-Hanafi dispute where the strict qiyas ruling (invalidity) is set aside in favor of a more practical ruling based on customary practice, following Abu Yusuf's view.

Key Terms
رفاع (rafa'): Carrying the harvested crop to the threshing floor (al-baydar).
دياسة (diyasah): Threshing, i.e., treading the crop with cattle to separate the grain from the stalks.
تذرية (tadhriyah): Winnowing, i.e., throwing the threshed mixture into the air so that the wind separates the grain from the chaff.
جداد (jidad): Picking dates from palm trees, distinguished from harvesting (حصاد) which is for grains.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in this passage, can the worker be required to pay for expenses and carry the crop to his home?
A) No, it invalidates the contract.
B) Yes, because of prevalent custom.
C) Only if the contract explicitly states it.
D) It is forbidden under all circumstances.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, custom can override qiyas in muzara'ah contracts, but only for works that are actually customary; works like picking dates that lack custom are not permissible.

Invalidating Conditions in Muzara'ah Contract
Explains which work conditions invalidate sharecropping contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on stipulating post-harvest work in muzara'ah and apply the principle that custom ('urf) can override qiyas to determine contract validity.

Core Idea
Custom can override qiyas: Abu Yusuf's view on stipulating post-harvest work becomes the operative ruling.

In sharecropping (muzara'ah), the basic contract obligates the worker (amil) to cultivate the land. But what if the parties also stipulate post-harvest tasks like threshing and winnowing on the worker? The Hanafi school has an internal split: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider such conditions invalidating, while Abu Yusuf permits them if customary. This lesson unpacks the dispute and shows how later Hanafi practice relied on custom as a source of flexibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed conditions
List the post-harvest activities mentioned in the passage: harvesting (hisad), carrying (rifa'), threshing (diyasah), and winnowing (tadhriyah). These are extraneous to cultivation work.
The passage defines each term to clarify what is being stipulated.
2
State the original Hanafi ruling and its proof
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that stipulating these tasks invalidates the contract (fasid). Their proof: the contract only requires cultivation work; post-harvest tasks are extraneous, like carrying and grinding, and stipulating them corrupts the contract by qiyas.
This is the ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah (Imam Muhammad).
3
Present Abu Yusuf's position and its basis
Abu Yusuf allows the stipulation if it is customary among people. His proof: custom ('urf) establishes a precedent that overrides qiyas. This is istihsan based on social practice.
The passage quotes Al-Multaqa: 'the fatwa is upon it' and mentions the scholars of Balkh.
4
Explain the tarjih and the role of custom
Later authorities like Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani chose Abu Yusuf's view as the most correct (al-asahh). The ruling becomes mufta bihi: the contract is valid if the stipulated work is customary.
This shows how the Hanafi school uses 'urf as a source of law, especially in transactions.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If the parties stipulate post-harvest tasks and there is no custom, the contract is invalid. If custom exists, it is valid. The passage adds that if the stipulation lacks custom (e.g., harvest by a third party), it is invalid by consensus.
The thamarah al-khilaf: the ruling changes based on the presence or absence of custom.

كأجر الحصاد والرفاع والدياسة والتذرية فإن شرطاه على العامل فسدت

Book of Sharecropping. Rulings of Sharecropping: Like the wages of harvesting, carrying, threshing, and winnowing; if they stipulate them upon the worker, the contract becomes corrupt. = (Harvesting) is cutting the crop. It is contracted from the sharecropper's side, so it is specific to him. Whatever is after the completion of the crop is upon both according to their shares. Whatever is after the expiry of the term before ripening is also upon both. Whatever is after division is upon each one in his share because each one's share has been distinguished. (Supplement, al-Fath with addition). Al-Rifā‘: carrying the crop after harvest to the threshing floor. [Ramz al-Haqā’iq: 2/357] Al-Diyāsah: from daws, which is treading the crop with cattle to extract the grain. [Ramz al-Haqā’iq: 2/357] Al-Tadhriyah: from dharā, winnowing in the air to extract the grain and separate the chaff. [Ramz al-Haqā’iq: 2/357] 'If they stipulate both, etc.' means: if they stipulate the work that occurs after the completion of the crop, like harvesting and what we mentioned, upon the worker, the sharecropping becomes corrupt because it is a condition not required by the contract. We only say that because the contract requires the worker's work, and these things are not among the actions of cultivation, so they are extraneous. Thus, stipulating them corrupts the contract, like stipulating carrying and grinding upon the worker. (Supplement to al-Bahr al-Rā’iq: 8/322) It is narrated from Abū Yūsuf that it is permissible. He said in al-Multaqā: 'Upon it is the fatwā, and the scholars of Balkh gave fatwā accordingly and said: stipulating expenses and carrying to his house upon the worker is also permissible due to custom among people, and qiyās is abandoned for it.' And Shams al-A’immah chose it and said it is the most correct. And if they stipulate the harvest (al-jidād) upon the worker and the harvesting (al-ḥiṣād) upon someone else, it is not permissible by consensus due to lack of custom. (Supplement, al-Fath)
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This is a detailed ruling on invalidating conditions in a muzara‘ah (sharecropping) contract. The passage first defines key post-harvest activities: cutting (ḥiṣād), carrying (rifā‘), threshing (diyāsah), and winnowing (tadhriyah). The ruling is: if the parties stipulate these tasks upon the worker (the one who cultivates), the contract becomes invalid (fāsid). The reasoning given is that the contract only obligates the worker's labor related to cultivation (e.g., sowing, tending). Post-harvest work, like threshing and winnowing, is not part of cultivation; it is extraneous. Stipulating such extraneous work invalidates the contract, similar to stipulating carrying the grain home or grinding it. However, a narration from Abu Yusuf allows it. The fatwa according to the 'Multaqā' and the scholars of Balkh is that it is permissible if there is a custom (ta‘āmul) among people to include such tasks, overriding qiyās. Imam Shams al-A’immah al-Halwāni considered this the more correct view. This shows the Hanafi principle of using custom ('urf) as a basis for istiḥsān. But if the stipulated work has no customary basis (like harvesting by someone else), it is invalid by consensus.

Key Terms
الرفاع (al-rifā‘): Carrying the harvested crop to the threshing floor.
الدياسة (al-diyāsah): Threshing by treading animals to separate grain from stalks.
التذرية (al-tadhriyah): Winnowing in the air to separate grain from chaff.
المزارعة (al-muzāra‘ah): A contract of sharecropping where one party provides land and the other works it, sharing the crop.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi ruling if the parties stipulate threshing work on the worker in a muzara'ah contract?
A) The contract is invalid regardless.
B) The contract is valid if such stipulation is customary.
C) The contract is valid only if the worker agrees voluntarily after the contract.
D) The contract is invalid unless the landowner does the work.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi muzara'ah, stipulating post-harvest work on the worker is invalid by Zahir al-Riwayah, but custom can override this, making the contract valid—a clear example of istihsan overriding qiyas.

Musaqah: Definition and Ruling with Intra-Hanafi Differences
Defines musaqah and its ruling with intra-Hanafi differences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of musaqah, explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on its validity, list the four differences between musaqah and muzara'ah, and apply the rule on term specification.

Core Idea
Musaqah is valid per the Sahibayn; fatwa is on their view, with four key differences from sharecropping.

Musaqah is a contract for tending trees in exchange for a share of fruit. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement: Abu Hanifa invalidated it like sharecropping, but the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) permitted it, and the fatwa follows them. This lesson clarifies the definition and the unique conditions that distinguish musaqah from muzara'ah.

Guided Path
1
Define musaqah linguistically and legally
Identify the linguistic root (saqa) and the legal definition: a contract to hand over trees to a worker for a share of fruit. Note the similarity to muzara'ah.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
State that Abu Hanifa does not permit musaqah (like muzara'ah), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad permit it. The fatwa is on their view.
This is an exception to the general rule that Abu Hanifa's view is usually followed.
3
List the four differences from muzara'ah
Go through each difference: (1) no compulsion to proceed, (2) no rent after term expiry, (3) different compensation if trees are claimed, (4) no need to specify term.
These differences arise because musaqah is less essential and the fruit ripening time is predictable.
4
Apply the rule on term specification
Understand why musaqah does not require a fixed term (istihsan due to known ripening), unlike muzara'ah. Note the exception for saplings that have not yet fruited.
This is a practical difference: musaqah can be open-ended for mature trees.

Source Text

كتاب المساقاة
كتاب المساقاة
تعريف المساقاة وحكمها
مفاعلة من السقي لغة
هي معاقدة دفع الأشجار إلى من يعمل فيها على أن الثمر بينهما، وهي كالمزارعة،
الشرع
المساقاة
تصح في النخل والشجر والكرم والرطاب وأصول الباذنجان. فإن دفع نخلا فيه ثمرة أي المساقاة
مساقاة، والثمرة تزيد بالعمل صحت،
على وجه المساقات و الحال أن الثمرة
كتاب المساقاة
وجه
المساقاة
المناسبة بين الكتابين ظاهر؛ لأن كلا منهما عقد شرع لتحصيل منفعة الملك، ولهذا كانت كالمزارعة حكما وخلافا وشروطا إلا أن حق المساقاة كان أن تقدم على المزارعة؛ لكثرة من يقول بجواز المساقاة، ولورود الأحاديث في معاملة النبي عليه أهل خيبر، لكن قدم المزارعة؛ لشدة الحاجة إلى معرفة أحكامها، وكثرة تفاريع مسائلها. فتح بتصرف)
وهي كالمزارعة إلخ يعني لا يجوز عند الإمام ويجوز عندهما، والفتوى على قولهما. وشروطها عندهما شروط المزارعة إلا في أربعة أشياء: أحدها: إذا امتنع أحدهما عن المضي لا يجبر؛ لأنه لا ضرر عليه في المضي، بخلاف المزارعة على ما تقدم. الثاني: إذا انقضت المدة تترك بلا أجرة بخلاف المزارعة الثالث: إذا استحق النخل يرجع العامل بأجرة مثله، والمزارع بقيمة الزرع الرابع: في بيان المدة، فإذا لم يبين المدة فيها يجوز استحسانا؛ لأن وقت إدراك الثمرة معلوم، وقلما يتفاوت فيه، فيدخل ما هو المتيقن به وإدراك البذر في أصول الرطبة هذا بمنزلة إدراك الثمار؛ لأن لها نهاية معلومة، فلا يشترط فيها بيان المدة، بخلاف الزرع؛ لأن ابتداءه يختلف، والانتهاء يبتني عليه، فتدخله الجهالة الفاحشة، وبخلاف ما إذا دفع إليه غرسا معاملة، وقد نبت ولم يثمر بعد معاملة حيث لا يجوز إلا ببيان المدة؛ لأنه يتفاوت بقوة الأرض وضعفها تفاوتا فاحشا، فلا يمكن صرفه إلى أول ثمرة تخرج منه تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٢٤/٨] وتصح في النخل إلخ أي تصح المساقات عندهما في جميع هذه الأشياء، وقال الشافعي في الجديد: لا تجوز إلا في النخل والكرم، ولا تجوز المزارعة إلا تبعا للمساقات بأن يكون النخيل والكرم في أرض بيضاء يسقى بماء النخيل، فيأمر بأن تزرع الأرض أيضا بالنصف، ودليله في حصر الجواز في النخيل والكرم: أن جوازها بحديث خيبر، وهو مخصوص فلا يتعدى، وأنه عليها عامل أهل خيبر بشطر ما يخرج من ثمر أو زرع، رواه البخاري ومسلم وآخرون، وهذا مطلق فلا يجوز تقييده ببعض الأشجار دون بعض. واعلم أن قوله : "النخل" لم يأخذه الشراح في المتن ولا هو في جميع النسخ المطبوعة، ولكنه في النسخة الأحمدية، ونقل في هذا الكتاب منه. (من عيني، فتح بزيادة من المحشي والرطاب إلخ [جمع رطبة وهي التي تسميها المصريون البريسم، والمراد بها هنا جميع البقول وإنما خص الرطاب وأصول الباذنجان بالذكر تنبيها على أنهما من أنواع الشجر؛ لأن الشجر اسم لما له ساق ولهما ساق. رمز الحقائق: ٣٥٨/٢]
Book of Musaqah. Book of Musaqah. Definition and Ruling of Musaqah: It is a verbal noun from 'watering' in language. In law, it is a contract of handing over trees to someone who works on them on the condition that the fruit is between them, and it is like sharecropping. Musaqah is valid for date palms, trees, grapevines, fresh herbs (al-riṭāb), and stalks of eggplant. If he hands over a palm tree that has fruit as a musaqah, and the fruit increases with work, it is valid... The appropriateness between the two books is apparent because each is a contract prescribed for obtaining benefit of property, thus it is like sharecropping in ruling, disagreement, and conditions, except that musaqah should have been presented before sharecropping due to the many who say it is permissible and due to the hadiths about the Prophet's transaction with the people of Khaybar, but sharecropping was presented due to the strong need to know its rulings and the abundance of its branches. (al-Fatḥ with adaptation) 'It is like sharecropping, etc.' means: it is not valid according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) but is valid according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and the fatwa is on their view. Its conditions according to them are the conditions of sharecropping except in four things: One: If one of them refrains from proceeding, he is not compelled because there is no harm in proceeding, unlike sharecropping as previously mentioned. Two: When the term expires, it is left without rent, unlike sharecropping. Three: If the palm trees are claimed (by a third party), the worker gets the equivalent wage, and the landowner gets the value of the crop. Four: Regarding specification of the term; if the term is not specified in it, it is valid as istihsan because the time of ripening of the fruit is known and rarely varies, so what is certain enters. And the germination of seeds in the roots of fresh herbs is like the ripening of fruits because they have a known limit, so specifying the term is not required, unlike crops because their beginning varies and the end depends on it, so gross ignorance enters. And unlike if he handed over to him a sapling as a transaction, and it has grown but not yet fruited, where it is not valid except with specifying the term because it varies greatly with the strength or weakness of the land, so it cannot be directed to the first fruit that emerges. (Supplement to al-Bahr al-Rā’iq: 8/324) 'And it is valid for date palms, etc.' means: musaqah is valid according to them for all these things. Al-Shāfi‘ī said in his new view: it is not valid except for date palms and grapevines, and sharecropping is not valid except as a subsidiary to musaqah when the date palms and grapevines are in white land irrigated with the water of the date palms, so he orders that the land also be planted for half. His evidence for restricting permissibility to date palms and grapevines is that its permissibility is based on the hadith of Khaybar, which is specific, so it is not extended. And that the Prophet contracted with the people of Khaybar for half of what comes out of fruit or crop, narrated by Bukhari and Muslim and others, and this is absolute, so it cannot be restricted to some trees without others. Know that his statement 'date palms' was not taken by the commentators in the text and is not in all printed copies, but it is in the Aḥmadiyya copy, and it is transmitted from it in this book. (From ‘Aynī, al-Fatḥ with additions from the annotator: 'and fresh herbs, etc.' [plural of riṭbah, which the Egyptians call barīsim; what is meant here is all vegetables. He specifically mentioned fresh herbs and stalks of eggplant to alert that they are types of trees, because 'tree' is a name for what has a trunk, and both have trunks. Ramz al-Ḥaqā’iq: 2/358]
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage introduces the book of Musaqah (watering contract). It defines musaqah as a verbal noun from 's-q-y' (to water) linguistically, and legally as a contract where trees are handed to a worker who tends them, and the fruit is shared between owner and worker. It states that musaqah is similar to sharecropping (muzara‘ah) in many rulings, but also has key differences. The ruling: per Abu Hanifa, musaqah is not valid (he considers it a form of invalid sharecropping), but it is valid according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and the fatwa is on their view. The text then lists four differences from sharecropping: (1) no compulsion to proceed if one party refuses, (2) when term expires, land is left without rent, (3) if a third party claims the trees, the worker gets wages and owner gets crop value, (4) specifying the term is not needed for musaqah because fruit ripening time is generally known, unlike crops which vary. Then it addresses validity for various plants: palm trees, trees (including vines), fresh herbs (like Egyptian barisim/clover), and eggplant stalks. It then engages with al-Shafi‘i’s view that musaqah is only valid for date palms and grapevines, based on the hadith of Khaybar. The Hanafi response is that the hadith is absolute and not restricted, so it applies to all fruit-bearing trees. Finally, it notes that the word 'date palms' (al-nakhl) in the text may be a later addition not in all manuscripts.

Key Terms
المساقاة (al-musāqāh): A contract where trees are given to a worker to tend in exchange for a share of the fruit.
المزارعة (al-muzāra‘ah): Sharecropping; a contract for cultivating land in exchange for a share of the crop.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi musaqah contract, if one party refuses to proceed, what is the ruling?
A) Both parties are compelled to proceed.
B) Only the worker is compelled.
C) Neither is compelled.
D) Only the owner is compelled.

Key Takeaway
Musaqah is a valid contract per Sahibayn; its conditions mirror muzara'ah except in four key areas: non-compulsion, no rent after term, special compensation, and no need to specify term for mature trees.

Scope of Musaqah: Valid Plants and the Shafi‘i Dispute
Discusses which plants musaqah is valid for and the Shafi'i dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the plants for which musaqah is valid according to the Hanafi school, explain the Shafi‘i restriction, analyze the Hanafi response based on the hadith of Khaybar, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Hanafis permit musaqah on all fruit-bearing trees and vines; Shafi‘is restrict to date palms and grapevines.

The hadith of Khaybar is the primary evidence for musaqah, but scholars differ on its scope. The Hanafi school applies it broadly to all trees, vegetables with stalks, and even eggplant. Imam al-Shafi‘i limits it to date palms and grapevines. This lesson unpacks the dispute and the Hanafi argument based on the absolute (mutlaq) nature of the hadith.

Guided Path
1
List the plants for which musaqah is valid in the Hanafi school
From the text: date palms, other trees (like fruit trees), grapevines, fresh herbs (al-riṭāb, meaning all vegetables), and stalks of eggplant. Understand that 'tree' includes anything with a trunk.
The mention of fresh herbs and eggplant is to illustrate that they have trunks, so they are considered trees.
2
Identify the Shafi‘i restriction
Imam al-Shafi‘i (in his new view) only permits musaqah for date palms and grapevines. Sharecropping is only valid as a subsidiary to musaqah for these plants.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof from the hadith of Khaybar
The hadith states that the Prophet contracted with the people of Khaybar for half of the fruit and crop. The Hanafi school argues this hadith is absolute (mutlaq) and not restricted to specific plants, so it applies to all fruit-bearing trees.
The opposing view is that the hadith is specific to the context of Khaybar.
4
Understand the Hanafi response and thamarah al-khilaf
The Hanafi response is that the hadith cannot be restricted without evidence. The practical consequence: Hanafis allow musaqah on any fruit-bearing tree, while Shafi‘is only on palms and vines.
This is a clear example of how usul principles (mutlaq vs muqayyad) affect fiqh rulings.

Source Text

Know that his statement 'date palms' was not taken by the commentators in the text and is not in all printed copies, but it is in the Aḥmadiyya copy, and it is transmitted from it in this book. (From ‘Aynī, al-Fatḥ with additions from the annotator: 'and fresh herbs, etc.' [plural of riṭbah, which the Egyptians call barīsim; what is meant here is all vegetables. He specifically mentioned fresh herbs and stalks of eggplant to alert that they are types of trees, because 'tree' is a name for what has a trunk, and both have trunks. Ramz al-Ḥaqā’iq: 2/358]
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage introduces the book of Musaqah (watering contract). It defines musaqah as a verbal noun from 's-q-y' (to water) linguistically, and legally as a contract where trees are handed to a worker who tends them, and the fruit is shared between owner and worker. It states that musaqah is similar to sharecropping (muzara‘ah) in many rulings, but also has key differences. The ruling: per Abu Hanifa, musaqah is not valid (he considers it a form of invalid sharecropping), but it is valid according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and the fatwa is on their view. The text then lists four differences from sharecropping: (1) no compulsion to proceed if one party refuses, (2) when term expires, land is left without rent, (3) if a third party claims the trees, the worker gets wages and owner gets crop value, (4) specifying the term is not needed for musaqah because fruit ripening time is generally known, unlike crops which vary. Then it addresses validity for various plants: palm trees, trees (including vines), fresh herbs (like Egyptian barisim/clover), and eggplant stalks. It then engages with al-Shafi‘i’s view that musaqah is only valid for date palms and grapevines, based on the hadith of Khaybar. The Hanafi response is that the hadith is absolute and not restricted, so it applies to all fruit-bearing trees. Finally, it notes that the word 'date palms' (al-nakhl) in the text may be a later addition not in all manuscripts.

Key Terms
المساقاة (al-musāqāh): A contract where trees are given to a worker to tend in exchange for a share of the fruit.
الرطاب (al-riṭāb): Fresh herbs, specifically clover (barisim in Egyptian usage), but meant generically for vegetables.
النخل (al-nakhl): Date palms.
الكرم (al-karm): Grapevines.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a valid plant for a musaqah contract?
A) Date palms
B) Grapevines
C) Wheat fields
D) Eggplant stalks

Key Takeaway
Hanafis extend musaqah to all plants with a trunk, citing the absolute hadith of Khaybar, while Shafi'is restrict it to date palms and grapevines.

Mosaqat Invalid When Fruit Growth Has Ended
Ruling and proof for invalidity of musaqat after fruit ripening

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that musaqat is invalid when fruit no longer benefits from labor, and apply the exception from Qadi Khan when preservation work is still needed.

Core Idea
Musaqat invalid when fruit ripe; labor is basis of reward.

This lesson explores a critical boundary of the musaqat contract. While musaqat is generally valid by istihsan for trees needing annual care, its validity depends on the fruit still benefiting from work. Once the fruit has fully ripened and no longer responds to labor, the contract becomes invalid—otherwise the worker would earn without effort. However, a later refinement by Qadi Khan creates an important exception: if preservation (e.g., guarding) is still required, the contract can remain valid. We will trace the proof structure and understand the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making a musaqat contract when the fruit is already ripe and no longer benefits from work. The ruling is that the contract is invalid (la tasihh) – it is batil.
The text explicitly states: 'إن انتهت الثمرة... لا تصح المساقاة'.
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is that the worker only deserves reward by work, and after ripening no work has any effect. The permissibility before ripening was an exception based on need (istihsan), contrary to the original analogy (qiyas).
The text says: 'لأن العامل لا يستحق إلا بالعمل، ولا أثر للعمل بعد التناهي'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The proof is that giving reward without work is not permitted by Islamic law. Since after ripening the worker's labor does not benefit the fruit, any reward would be unjust.
The text says: 'فلو جاز بعد الإدراك لا يستحق إلا بلا عمل ولم يرد به الشرع'.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (exception)
Qadi Khan (as cited in al-Fath) allows the contract if preservation work (e.g., guarding) is still needed, even after ripening. This refines the absolute statement in the matn.
The exception is for cases where without guarding the fruit would be lost.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position adopts Qadi Khan's exception. Thus the ruling is not absolute: if preservation is necessary, the contract remains valid.
Later fatwa works consider the exception operative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن انتهت لا: إن انتهت الثمرة بأن صارت رطبا ولا تزيد بالعمل لا تصح المساقات؛ لأن العامل لا يستحق إلا بالعمل، ولا أثر للعمل بعد التناهي، فلو جاز بعد الإدراك لا يستحق إلا بلا عمل ولم يرد به الشرع، ولا يجوز إلحاقه بما قبل التناهي؛ لأن جوازه قبل التناهي للحاجة على خلاف القياس، ولا حاجة إلى مثله فبقي على الأصل. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٢٣/٨] قال في "الفتح": نقل شيخنا عن قاضي خان ما نصه رجل دفع إلى رجل كرما، معاملة، وفيه أشجار لا تحتاج إلى العمل سوى الحفظ قالوا إن كان بحال لو لم يحفظ تذهب ثمرتها جازت المعاملة، فاستفيد من كلام قاضي خان أن ما في المتن من قوله: "وإن انتهت لا" ليس على إطلاقه بل يحمل على ما إذا كانت الثمرة غير محتاجة للسقي أو الحفظ. (ملخصا من الفتح) كالمزارعة إلخ : يعني إذا زارع الزرع، وهو بقل جاز، وإن أدرك واستحصد لم يجز. رمز الحقائق: ٣٥٨/٢]
And if it has ended, no: If the fruit has ended by becoming ripe and does not increase with work, then the musaqat is not valid; because the worker does not deserve anything except by work, and there is no effect of work after cessation. So if it were permissible after ripening, he would deserve only without work, and the law has not permitted that. It cannot be analogized to before cessation because its permissibility before cessation was for need, contrary to analogy, and there is no need for the like, so it remains on the original principle. Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 8/323. He said in al-Fath: Our teacher reported from Qadi Khan: A man gave a vineyard to another on a mu'amala basis, and in it there were trees that did not need work except guarding. They said: If it were such that if he did not guard, the fruit would be lost, then the mu'amala is valid. So it is derived from Qadi Khan's speech that what is in the text: "And if it has ended, no" is not absolute but is interpreted for when the fruit does not need irrigation or guarding. (Summarized from al-Fath) "Like muzara'a" etc.: Meaning if he made a muzara'a contract on the crop while it is a seedling, it is valid, but if it has ripened and is ready for harvest, it is not valid. Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/358.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the invalidity of musaqat (sharecropping of trees) when the fruit has fully ripened and no longer benefits from further work. The author explains that the worker only deserves payment for work, and after ripening, no work affects the fruit, so the contract would give reward without work, which is not permitted. The general rule is that musaqat is valid by istihsan (juridicial preference) before ripening due to need, but after ripening the original analogy (qiyas) of prohibition applies. An exception from Qadi Khan is cited: if the fruit still needs preservation (e.g., guarding), the contract remains valid. The passage ends by analogizing to muzara'a (crop sharecropping): if the crop is already mature when the contract is made, the contract is invalid. This illustrates that the ruling is based on the absence of need for the worker's labor.

Key Terms
المساقاة (al-musaqat): A contract where a worker tends fruit trees in exchange for a share of the fruit.
انتهت الثمرة (intahat al-thamara): The fruit has fully ripened and no longer benefits from additional labor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of a musaqat contract if the fruit is already ripe and does not need further work?
A) The contract is valid and the worker gets a share of the fruit.
B) The contract is invalid because the worker would earn without work.
C) The contract is valid only if the worker is a Muslim.
D) The contract is valid if the fruit still needs guarding.

Key Takeaway
Musaqat is invalid when the fruit no longer benefits from work, unless preservation is still required.
